The Accession of the New British Monarch George VI; Proclamation Read by the Privy Council; Ministers Swear Allegiance 51

(London) This morning at St. James's Palace, in the presence of the Accession Council, George VI was formally proclaimed King of Great Britain and Emperor of India. When the new monarch arrived at the palace, he was wearing the uniform of an Admiral of the Fleet. He slowly ascended the red and yellow throne. Those attending the ceremony were all dressed in formal attire or official uniforms, creating a rather grand spectacle. Guests were welcomed by the Duke of Norfolk. Nearly all three hundred members of the Privy Council were in attendance. Among the first to arrive were Prime Minister Baldwin and the Lord Mayor of London.

Those present openly proclaimed: "We, therefore, with one heart and one soul, and with the blessing of God, do hereby proclaim Prince Albert Frederick Arthur George to be King, by the title of George VI. To whom we do acknowledge all faith and all obedience with humble affection; beseeching God by whom Kings and Queens do reign, to bless His Majesty with long and happy Years to reign over us."

Subsequently, members of the Privy Council, as well as representatives from various Dominions and India, swore allegiance. A new Privy Council was then formed. The first act of the new monarch upon accession was, according to custom, to issue a decree to the Privy Council. Following this, he took an oath to safeguard the security of the Church of Scotland.

The proclamation of the new monarch and the swearing of allegiance commenced this morning and were broadcast via radio throughout the Empire. Sunday marks the new monarch's forty-first birthday, and many places throughout the Empire have announced a day of holiday. Tomorrow, churches will offer prayers for the new King George VI and the Empire.

This afternoon, when the new monarch was proclaimed, the number of spectators was even greater than during the accession of the abdicated King Edward VIII in January of this year. Despite the cold weather, many people took advantage of the Saturday half-day holiday to visit. At 3:00 PM, the Lord Chamberlain stood on the balcony of St. James's Palace and read the proclamation of the new monarch's accession. This proclamation was also read separately at the Exchange and three other locations.

According to official sources, the coronation of the new King George VI and the new Queen Elizabeth is scheduled for May 12th of next year, which is the date originally set for the coronation of the abdicated king. (Reuters and Havas, 12th)

(London) It is not yet known when the new King and Queen will move to Buckingham Palace. Public opinion suggests that the King will follow the practice of the previous King and visit the palace daily for several months to handle state affairs after his accession. The new King and Queen had previously decided to spend Christmas with the Queen Mother at Sandringham. Newspapers now believe that this plan will not be changed due to the accession. The new King's schedule for the coming year is a matter of great concern to both the government and the public. To what extent the new King will follow the schedule set by the previous King is a topic of much discussion. There is good reason to expect that the new King will formally tour India next winter, according to the previous King's plans.

The House of Commons is scheduled to convene this afternoon to swear allegiance to the new King. The adjournment of today's session will be early. This ceremony will be completed next Monday.

The Prime Minister will bring the new King's edict to the House of Commons on Monday evening and will propose a response. On Tuesday, the House of Commons will resume its regular business and is scheduled to adjourn on the 18th for the Christmas holidays. (Reuters, 12th)

(London) The new Queen Elizabeth, originally named Elizabeth Angela Marguerite Bowes-Lyon, is the daughter of the Earl of Strathmore and Kinghorne, a noble Scottish family with fourteen generations of distinguished ancestors. She is the third daughter and was born in London on August 4, 1900. On April 26, 1923, she married the Duke of York. The British people greatly admire her because their union was based on love, not on considerations of social status. The Queen has two daughters. The elder, Elizabeth, was born on April 21, 1926, and is now the heir apparent. The younger, Margaret Rose, was born on August 21, 1930. The Queen is known for being kind and approachable, without any pretense, and is deeply loved by the British and the people of the British Empire. She is most popular for her ability to manage her household well and is considered a virtuous wife and mother. (Havas, 12th)

The New British Monarch George VI, the Queen, and the Princesses

The New British Monarch Named George VI, Following the Will of Victoria 52

(London) According to official sources, the new monarch's title has been decided as George VI, and not Albert I. This is because Queen Victoria, during her reign, had a husband named Albert and specifically instructed that the name Albert should not be used as a monarchical title in the future. This time, the new King's accession and change to George VI is in accordance with Victoria's will. (Havas, 11th)

The Abdicated King Leaves the Country by Ship; Issues a Farewell Address to the People; Farewell Banquet at Windsor Castle Last Night 53

Portsmouth The abdicated King Edward has departed the country aboard the destroyer HMS Fury after midnight. The Prince arrived by car, accompanied by one police car and two baggage cars. Upon arrival, he proceeded to the waterfront to board the ship and depart. The destroyer HMS Wakeful is also set to depart tonight, but the Prince did not transfer to that ship. According to the Daily Mail, the Prince is headed to Gibraltar. (National Telegram, 11th)

(London) The abdicated King Edward, now titled "Mr. Windsor," left the country early this morning. His whereabouts are kept secret, and no one knows where he is going. Last night, in his capacity as King, he approved the Act of Abdication, which was his final act as monarch. A few hours later, he traveled by car to Portsmouth and boarded a destroyer. Half an hour later, the ship set sail, escorted by the destroyer HMS Wolfertone, which carried many pieces of luggage. It is reported that "Mr. Windsor" is accompanied by his Equerry, Lieutenant Colonel Piers Legh, who is also his private detective and a member of the royal household. The abdicated king arrived at Portsmouth from Windsor Castle by car after midnight. The car curtains were drawn, and several other cars, laden with luggage, followed behind. His attendants waited for him at the dock. Dock officials were sworn to secrecy regarding the abdicated King's movements and destination. However, HMS Wolfertone had already been prepared and was awaiting him. As the abdicated King's car passed through the dock entrance, the ship quietly pulled alongside the pier. The police officers on duty, clearly aware of who was in the car, allowed it to enter without hindrance. No one was allowed to enter with the car. It was heard that before the abdicated King boarded the HMS Trenchant yacht, he spoke briefly with Admiral Fisher. The battleship HMS Nelson was seen in the distance, illuminated by electric lights, and the cruiser HMS Neptune was also docked nearby. While the luggage was being loaded onto HMS Wolfertone, the ship's crew was extremely active. The abdicated King held a farewell banquet at Windsor Castle last night, attended by his younger brother, the new King George VI, his mother, Queen Mary, his younger brother, the Duke of Gloucester, his uncle, the Duke of Athlone, and several princesses. Those present felt a deep sense of sadness and farewell. The new Queen Elizabeth was unable to attend due to a mild cold and the cold weather. (Reuters, 12th)

(London) After delivering a farewell address to the nation via radio last night, the abdicated King Edward hurriedly said goodbye to his relatives and old friends. He then quietly left London by car with his adjutant, Captain Piers Legh. At that time, the car traveled through the suburbs, and all was silent. The person in the car was alone and solitary. His departure, wherever he may go, is like a wild cloud or a free crane, which is much more carefree than those who manage countless affairs of state every day. Around midnight, the car arrived at the "Unicorn Gate" of the Portsmouth Naval Dockyard. Local officials had been instructed in advance to maintain strict secrecy regarding the abdicated King's visit. The abdicated King shook hands and bid farewell to Admiral Fisher, the commander of the fortress. The Admiral, overcome with emotion, could not help but shed tears. At that time, it was late at night, and only a few naval soldiers held electric torches. Three cruisers were anchored outside the harbor, with their lights flickering faintly. Soon after, Admiral Fisher escorted the abdicated King away from the fortress headquarters and quietly boarded the ship. (Havas, 12th)

The New Monarch Confers the Title of Duke of Windsor on the Abdicated King 54

(London) Today, the new King George VI conferred the title of Duke of Windsor on the abdicated King Edward. If the abdicated King marries Mrs. Simpson in the future, she will be styled as the Duchess of Windsor. (Reuters, 12th)

(London) According to reliable sources, the abdicated King is not going to Cannes, France, to meet Mrs. Simpson. Due to divorce law restrictions, Mrs. Simpson cannot meet with the abdicated King within five months. (Reuters, 12th)

(London) After approving the Act of Abdication, the abdicated King Edward quietly boarded a ship. In the evening, he went to Windsor Castle to be with the new King and the royal family, enjoying family happiness. At 10:29 PM, he departed. At approximately 10:00 PM, Windsor Castle staff announced to radio listeners, "His Royal Highness Prince Edward" will deliver a speech. The abdicated King then began his radio broadcast address, which was as follows:

"At long last I am able to say a few words of my own. I have never wanted to withhold anything, but until now, this has not been constitutionally possible. A few hours ago I discharged my last duty as King and Emperor, and now that I have been succeeded by my brother, the Duke of York, my first words must be to declare my allegiance to him. This I do with all my heart. You all know the reasons which have impelled me to renounce the throne. But I want you to understand that in making up my mind I did not forget the country or the Empire, which, as Prince of Wales and lately as King, I have always tried to serve. I have found it impossible to carry the heavy burden of responsibility and to discharge my duties as King as I would wish to do without the help and support of the woman I love. And I want you to understand that I have made this, the most serious decision of my life, only upon the single thought of what would in the end be best for all. This was a judgment which I myself had to make, and which I alone could make. The other person most nearly concerned has tried all she could to persuade me to take a different course. I have made this decision with calm and full deliberation, and it has been, as it has always been, the single object of my life, to serve my people as best I could. There has been no constitutional crisis or friction between me and Mr. Baldwin or between me and Dominion Prime Ministers." And finally, "Perhaps one day I may return. And until then God bless you all. God save the King!" (Havas, 11th)

Queen Mary Thanks Various Territories for Their Sincere Allegiance to the New Monarch 55

(London) Queen Mary has issued the following decree to the various territories of the Empire: "In this time of sorrow, looking at the circumstances around us, I cannot help but feel deeply moved. Therefore, I issue this decree to express my sincere gratitude to the people of the Empire. The death of the late King some time ago caused deep and immense pain. Less than a year has passed since then, and the grief has not yet left my heart. Now, another sudden change has occurred. How can I bear it? When my beloved son told me that he had to relinquish his responsibilities due to his duties, my motherly heart was broken. This situation need not be explained further. You all know how great a price my son paid for making this decision. In the past, my son served his country and the Empire with loyalty and diligence. You will never forget his virtues. Now, I especially recommend his younger brother, who unexpectedly and painfully acceded to the throne. I also urge you to give the new monarch as much loyalty as you gave to the late King and my eldest son. In this time of sorrow, I offer my most sincere prayers for the unity of our motherland and the Empire. May God bless our country, to become strong and prosperous. May He also bless you, guide you, and never abandon you." (Havas, 11th)

The Irish Free State Seizes the Opportunity to Amend its Constitution; Internal Affairs No Longer Use the King's Name; Relationship with the British Empire Not Severed 56

Dublin Today, the Parliament of the Irish Free State passed two motions proposed by President de Valera by a vote of 79 to 54. These motions stipulate amendments to the constitution, effectively making the Irish Free State a republic in its internal affairs. The President explained that this clause, which restricts the King's power, would bring the law in line with the facts. Opposition leader Cosgrave then raised questions, to which the President replied that since Article 1 of the constitution had not been changed, the relationship between the Free State and the British Empire had not been severed. (National Telegram, 11th)

Dublin The constitutional amendment bill for Southern Ireland proposed by Eamon de Valera, President of the Executive Council of the Irish Free State, at a special parliamentary session, passed this afternoon by a vote of seventy-nine to fifty-four. The bill stipulates the abolition of the post of Governor-General of Southern Ireland, and the removal of the name of the British monarch from all internal affairs of the Irish Free State. Governor-General of Ireland, Sir Harry Verney, has indicated to the British government that the Irish Free State cannot agree to the procedural clauses of the Statute of Westminster regarding constitutional disputes between Britain and the Dominions. Therefore, Sir Harry decided to submit two proposals regarding the Irish constitution and foreign affairs, recognizing the new monarch, but restricting the British monarch's role in the administration of the Irish Free State in the future. De Valera declared that since the Irish Free State is combined with Australia, Canada, New Zealand, and South Africa, and the British monarch is recognized by the aforementioned states, allowing them to appoint diplomatic and consular representatives and conclude international agreements, the Irish Free State will also recognize the British monarch's right to perform the same duties on behalf of the Irish Free State. The bill effectively means that the name of the British monarch will be removed from all internal political activities of the Irish Free State, retaining the British monarch's name only in matters of foreign affairs of the Irish Free State. As for the post of Governor-General, it will be abolished, and its duties will be assumed by the Speaker of Parliament. De Valera concluded by saying that the bill does not sever the relationship between the Irish Free State and the other federated states. (Reuters, 11th)

League of Nations Council Discusses Final Resolution Draft; Spain's Request Has a Just Reason; Supports French Mediation Proposal 58

(Geneva) The Council of the League of Nations held a closed-door meeting at 11:00 AM today, which ended at 1:30 PM. It drafted a final resolution on the Spanish issue and scheduled a public meeting at 6:00 PM to debate it. The resolution contains the following items:

(1) The Spanish government's application is based on Article 11 of the League of Nations Covenant, and its reason is entirely justified, as the Spanish Civil War is sufficient to cause a situation of international dispute.

(2) All countries should not interfere in the internal affairs of other countries, and countries should maintain good relations with each other regardless of the political system adopted within other countries.

(3) Reference to Article 10 of the Covenant, which stipulates that member states should respect each other's political independence and territorial integrity. However, the wording is implicit and does not clearly point out the facts.

(4) The Council approves the policy of non-intervention in the Spanish Civil War and supports the mediation proposal of Britain and France. The Council has rejected the proposal made by the Chilean representative that all personnel from the embassies and legations of various countries in Spain should be evacuated. However, the Chilean representative's proposal to find ways to humanize the Spanish Civil War has been included in the draft resolution. The League of Nations expects that the Council will vote on the draft resolution today and that there will be no difficulties. (Havas, 12th)

(Geneva) The Council of the League of Nations continued its meeting in the afternoon to discuss the Spanish situation. Lord Cranborne, Under-Secretary of State for Foreign Affairs of the United Kingdom, French Foreign Minister Yvon Delbos, the representative of New Zealand, the Soviet Ambassador to France Potemkin, and the Polish representative Komarnicki successively delivered speeches. Lord Cranborne first stated that the interference of some countries in the Spanish Civil War has seriously endangered international peace. He also stated that although the tasks of the Non-Intervention Committee have not been fully accomplished, they have been of great help in maintaining peace. "However, it is also true that some countries have failed to absolutely comply with the Non-Intervention Agreement, resulting in repeated instances of violating the agreement and assisting both sides of the civil war." He finally mentioned the recent proposal by Britain and France to the governments of Germany, Italy, Portugal, and the Soviet Union to jointly mediate the Spanish Civil War, stating that although some of these countries have not yet replied, the British government will request these countries to cooperate in promoting international peace. Following this, Yvon Delbos spoke, stating that the plan to monitor the import of armaments into Spain has been drafted and completed by the Adjustment Committee and submitted to the legitimate government of Spain and the Burgos authorities. This monitoring plan urgently needs to be implemented immediately. As for the principle of non-intervention in the Spanish Civil War, it must be expanded to include the prohibition of volunteers from going to Spain for assistance. He concluded by hoping that the Council would rise up and support the proposal of Britain and France to mediate the Spanish Civil War. At this point, the representative of New Zealand spoke, stating that since the Council has convened a meeting for the Spanish situation, it must take immediate action. Subsequently, Potemkin delivered a speech, stating that the Soviet Union has always faithfully complied with the restrictions of non-intervention in the Spanish Civil War and believes that in order to end the civil war in that country, the monitoring plan must be strictly implemented. Finally, he reiterated that the Soviet government has decided to participate in the proposal of the British and French governments and that the Council should support this proposal without reservation. However, the Polish representative Komarnicki stated that the Council must be very cautious and that any action that may cause new disputes should not be attempted lightly. He also said, "If the Council has not received a concrete application, it would be best to end the debate. Fortunately, Britain and France have already begun negotiations with the four most relevant countries, Germany, Italy, Portugal, and Russia." The Council adjourned at 7:25 PM and is scheduled to continue the meeting tomorrow afternoon. (Havas, 11th)

Britain Notifies the United States of the Suspension of War Debt Payments; Willing to Open Negotiations When Opportunity Arises 59

(Washington) The State Department announced today that Britain has formally notified it of the suspension of the war debt payment of $117,670,765 due on the 15th of this month. The British government also stated that it is willing to reopen negotiations at an appropriate time. However, State Department officials declared that the United States has not taken action to reopen negotiations. (National Telegram, 11th)

(Washington) British Ambassador to Washington Sir Ronald Lindsay delivered a reply from the British government to U.S. Under Secretary of State Sumner Welles today, stating that the war debt due on December 15th could not be paid. However, unlike previous notes, which stated that Britain was unable to pay the annual installments, this note stated, "The British government is willing to resume discussions with the United States when the opportunity arises to obtain a satisfactory result." Responsible parties here, considering the different wording of this year's note compared to those issued in previous years, hope that Britain will follow in France's footsteps and begin negotiating the war debt issue with the United States. The Finnish government has notified the U.S. government that it is willing to continue paying this year's installments. France had previously declared to the United States that it was willing to negotiate a settlement of the war debt issue, so the U.S. government is now waiting quietly for France to submit a solution. (Reuters, 11th)

France Expresses a Strong Attitude on the Spanish Issue; Non-Intervention Agreement Not Faithfully Fulfilled; Countries Will Reconsider Their Positions; Portugal Opposes Mediating the Civil War 60

(Geneva) French representative to the Council of the League of Nations Yvon Delbos recently made a statement to the press, roughly stating that the current goals of the French government regarding the Spanish issue are twofold: the non-intervention agreement must continue to be implemented, and the international monitoring measures must be strengthened. This is one goal. Mediation should be undertaken by the relevant countries to implement a ceasefire in Spain. This is the second goal. Delbos believes that France's intentions are fully in line with the spirit of the League of Nations Covenant and hopes that the League of Nations can support them. He also stated that in order to avoid international disputes, the governments of the relevant countries must act quickly. If some countries continue to supply arms and manpower to both sides of the Spanish Civil War, making the world regard the non-intervention agreement as a joke, then the great powers may have to reconsider their adopted positions. Wen Mary, Critically Ill for Months and Expected to Die Soon, Requests U.S. Court Permission to Return to Shanghai 64

Los Angeles, Wen Mary, a Shanghai woman of mixed race, was arrested for smuggling $50,000 worth of narcotics into the United States and found guilty after interrogation. She now suffers from severe tuberculosis and kidney disease and is expected to die within months. The judge presiding over the case was originally scheduled to pronounce sentence today, but has learned of her condition. Mary's sister, Dr. Wen Kangden, appeared in court today requesting permission for Mary to return to China. Mary also appeared in court today in a wheelchair, but was carried out of the courtroom by attendants during her sister's questioning by the judge to prevent her from hearing about her condition. The Instrument of Abdication of the British King Did Not Include "Defender of the Faith" 66

(London) In addition to "King of the United Kingdom and the Dominions beyond the Seas, Emperor of India," the title of the British monarch also includes "Defender of the Faith." International Commercial Telegram - December 12th Reuters Special Commercial Information 67

Gold and Silver

London Gold Price: Today is 141 shillings and 10 pence, up half a penny.

British-American: The London foreign exchange market was sluggish this morning. The British-American exchange rate opened at $4.9025, 0.03125 lower than yesterday's American-British closing rate. It fell 0.0625 an hour later to $4.901875, and remained unchanged thereafter.

Securities

The New York market this morning was mixed and sluggish. Operators seemed unwilling to make new trades at the end of the week. There was no selling pressure seen today, and prices mostly trended upward. Before 11:00 AM, the market showed some stability, and most security prices rose slightly. The market prices of various securities are listed on the left.

The Course of Shi Yushan's Defection; Wang Ying Also Sent Representatives to Guihua, Falsely Claiming to Surrender; Two-Thirds of Wang's Troops Followed Shi in Defecting 68

Special dispatch from Suiyuan: During the last counterattack on Bailingmiao, the puppet bandit army mainly used Wang Ying's bandit troops. A certain side used automobiles to transport all of Wang's bandits to Bailingmiao, then drove the automobiles away, intending to place them in a hopeless situation to strengthen their will to fight. However, the snowy ground there stretched as far as the eye could see, and there was a lack of clothing and food. Suffering from hunger and cold, the soldiers had no fighting spirit. After our army launched an attack, the bandits scurried away at the mere sight of us. Lei Zhongtian, the commander of Wang's bandit vanguard, is said to have been killed in action. After the defeat, Wang Ying only had small detachments remaining under Shi Yushan, Su Meilong, etc. Wang Ying himself, after repeated defeats, retreated to the vicinity of Wulanhua, intending to surrender to our side and cut off our advance towards Damiaozi. Considering that they were thinking of repenting, and not wanting to sacrifice the coerced compatriots, we did not attack them. However, according to investigations, Wang Ying's surrender was not sincere. On one hand, he sent people to a certain side to explain that he was reorganizing his troops and requested that that side replenish his guns and military supplies. On the other hand, he also sent people to contact our side about surrendering, but to no avail. On the morning of the 8th, our army advanced to the area of Caowa (on the road from Wulanhua to Damiaozi). Wang Ying actually ordered Shi Yushan to lead his troops to counterattack. Shi then requested Wang Ying to allocate him a battalion of artillery. After Wang agreed, Shi Yushan immediately led three and a half regiments of Wang's troops (Wang Regiment, Liu Regiment, Cao Regiment) and a company of artillery to surrender to our side. At 4:00 PM that afternoon, they arrived at Wulanhua and met with Zeng Yan-yi, Deputy Commander of the 35th Army, and Sun Changsheng, Commander of the Cavalry Division. The results of the talks were very satisfactory. It is said that after Shi Yushan's defection, two-thirds of Wang Ying's bandit troops followed Shi in defecting. Wang Ying's remaining bandits number less than one-third. According to one account, Wang Ying currently has no more than a company of remaining bandit troops. Seeing that the situation was hopeless, Wang Ying also urgently sent his Chief of Staff, Kou Ziyan, to Guihua on the afternoon of the 8th to meet with our military authorities to discuss surrendering sincerely. He hurriedly left Guihua to report to Wang Ying. It is said that Shi Yushan and others, who defected this time, plan to issue a circular telegram in the next few days, announcing the process of their defection and their aspiration to serve the country and eliminate the bandits from now on. Our side believes that the defection of Wang Ying's troops is equivalent to the victory at Bailingmiao. In addition to the soldiers being encouraged and delighted, they are even more invigorated, believing that the Chinese people ultimately belong to China. Although they may be temporarily oppressed and unable to be free, if there is an opportunity, their conscience will still not be extinguished. (9th)

Qingdao: Hints of Resolution in Sino-Japanese Negotiations; All Yarn Factories to Resume Work Uniformly on the 14th; Japanese Marines to Withdraw Within the Shortest Time 69

Qingdao correspondence, The illegal action of the Japanese Marines landing in Qingdao has been seriously negotiated by Mayor Shen Honglie to the Japanese Consul General in Qingdao. At first, the Japanese Marines not only refused to withdraw but also made unreasonable demands to the municipal government, almost reaching a stalemate. The newly appointed Commander-in-Chief of the Third Fleet, Hasegawa Kiyoshi, arrived in Qingdao but did not meet with Mayor Shen. He only summoned his subordinate captains, the Consul General, Military Attaché Tajiri, Chief of Special Services Hagi, etc., to hold an important meeting on the Izumo warship to discuss countermeasures. It is said that the Japanese side has made six demands to the municipal government, and Mayor Shen has sternly rejected those that exceed the scope. At the same time, the municipal government also made five demands to the Japanese side: (1) The Japanese consulate apologizes to the municipal government in writing for the illegal actions of the Japanese sailors landing; (2) Return the important documents taken from the Party headquarters; (3) Compensate for the losses suffered by the Chinese side; (4) Immediately withdraw the landed Japanese Marines; (5) Guarantee that such incidents will not happen again in the future. It is said that the Japanese Consul General has agreed to the above items. The municipal government has also agreed to consider accommodating the Japanese demands. This matter can probably be resolved peacefully. On the evening of the 10th, Shen also held the final decisive talks with the Japanese Consul General. Agreements were reached on the measures for the resumption of work by the yarn factories and other related matters. The Japan Textile Industry Association and the directors of various yarn factories also held a joint meeting at noon on the 10th, which lasted four hours. There was a detailed discussion on the issue of starting work. It is said that the factory side has decided to start work uniformly on the 14th, and all the Japanese Marines stationed in various factories will gradually withdraw to their ships before the 15th.

No Good Policy Yet for Anti-Smuggling in North China; Sun Weidong Returns North to Convey the Ministry of Finance's Opinions; Losses of Tianjin and Qinhuangdao Customs This Year Amount to 20 Million; False East Hebei Government Illegally Establishes False Inspection Offices 70

Tianjin Correspondence, The problem of anti-smuggling in North China is still pending resolution. After Sun Weidong, the Tianjin Customs Superintendent, returned north, he reported to Chairman Song in Beijing on the results of his consultations. If the Hebei-Chahar side has any suggestions, Sun will also forward them to the Ministry of Finance for further review and to develop an appropriate remedial measure. Therefore, the implementation of a new policy will be no earlier than next spring. Now, the opinions of the central government and the local governments are extremely consistent. That is, the previous misunderstandings have been completely eliminated through Sun Weidong's communication. When the Customs and the Directorate General of Smuggling Prevention for Road Transport are to promote anti-smuggling official duties in the future, the Hebei-Chahar authorities have already agreed to assist by local military and police agencies. However, before the diplomatic obstacles encountered by the Directorate General of Smuggling Prevention for Road Transport are resolved, it is still difficult to work in practice. Therefore, it is also difficult for Director General Pezzetta and Deputy Director Li Tonghua to come north for a while. Regarding the rumor that the Directorate General will move south, Sun Weidong solemnly denied it to the outside world after returning north. According to investigations from various parties, whether the Directorate General relocates depends on whether the anti-smuggling work can be carried out as desired and whether the diplomatic channels are opened. It seems premature to say that it is leaving now.

Since September of this year, after smugglers abandoned the use of railways and switched to highways, the rampant smuggling has been similar to the peak period in the spring and summer. On average, 100 to 150 truckloads of smuggled goods are shipped out of Tianjin every day. Recently, the weather has been cold, and the rivers have frozen over, cutting off shipping. Otherwise, dozens of civilian ships are also shipped out by water every day. The North-Ning Railway, faced with the situation, has to carry smuggled goods coming from the Eastern Hebei region. The Tianjin East Station Customs Anti-Smuggling Office has virtually abandoned its responsibilities in order to avoid trouble, allowing the ronin to transport the goods into a certain concession for storage. Therefore, the amount stored here is enough to be sold for more than half a year. In the future, the Bohai Bay will freeze, making it difficult for smuggled goods to land. Although there will be fewer coming, the smuggling in Tianjin is so much that it can still be sold as before. Therefore, the focus of anti-smuggling in the future lies in Tianjin. If Tianjin can effectively block smuggling, at least the areas of Eastern Hebei and Northern Shandong will not be harmed by the flood of smuggled goods. Due to the rampant smuggling, from January to the end of October this year, the customs revenue lost by the Tianjin and Qinhuangdao Customs amounts to more than 16 million yuan. Although the losses in November and December have not been calculated, it is estimated that they will each be around 1.6 to 1.7 million yuan. Therefore, the lowest loss of customs revenue in North China this year must be around 20 million yuan. Last year, the total revenue of the Tianjin and Qinhuangdao Customs was more than 39 million yuan. Compared to this year, the highest figure will probably not exceed 19 million yuan. Such a huge amount is truly heartbreaking.

Last year, the pseudo-East Hebei government illegally established pseudo-inspection offices in Beidaihe, Changli, and other places to collect import taxes on smuggled goods, called inspection fees. Starting in the spring of next year, it plans to use new regulations and revise the pseudo-tax rates. Not only will imported goods be taxed a quarter of the regular customs duties as inspection fees, but exported goods will also be released with reduced tax rates. As for its tax rules, they have been compiled using the pseudo-Manchukuo system and will be announced on New Year's Day. If there is still no solution to anti-smuggling in North China next spring, I am afraid that the rampant smuggling will be even worse than this year. The pseudo-organization has also forced British and American goods to take the path of smuggling recently. A notice was issued to British and American oil merchants that all types of oil sold in the Eastern Hebei region, regardless of whether they have paid Chinese customs duties, will be subject to a pseudo-inspection fee of 1.09 yuan per ten gallons (Chinese customs duty is 4.25 yuan per ten gallons). If unloaded at Qinhuangdao, it is not necessary to pay Chinese official taxes. Once the inspection fee is paid, it can be sold in the Eastern Hebei region. The oil merchants believe that the pseudo-government intentionally suppresses British and American oil merchants to help a certain country's private oil sales. In addition to requesting the Tianjin and Qinhuangdao Customs to find ways to stop this, they have also requested instructions from their respective head offices. Currently, the sales of British and American merchants in the pseudo-East Hebei region have been virtually abandoned. The customs authorities attach great importance to this matter and are waiting for the instructions of the Inspector General of Customs. (10th)

Song Zheyuan Declares Four Prerequisites—Speech at a Tea Party for the Press 71

Beiping Correspondence, The work of suppressing bandits in Suiyuan is gradually developing, and the situation in North China is becoming increasingly serious. Song Zheyuan, Chairman of the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Commission, is paying even more attention to the current situation. Having been in charge of military and political affairs in Hebei and Chahar for nearly a year, he specially hosted a tea party for the press at the Political Affairs Commission's East Building at 10:00 AM on the 10th to report on the political situation of the past year and the attitude and direction of the future towards the current situation. More than 50 reporters attended. Qin Dechun, Jia Deyao, Liu Zhizhou, Deng Zhexi, Lei Sishang, Wang Shijiu, and Guo Zhihan were all in attendance to welcome them. It lasted for an hour before adjourning. The following is a record of Song's speech:

"I, Zheyuan, have been entrusted to preside over military and political affairs in Hebei and Chahar for nearly a year. During this year, although I have often met with you in the press, I have had few opportunities to speak freely due to the many political affairs. Now, at the end of the year, I have specially prepared tea and snacks to invite you to gather together to express my respect and to encourage each other and work hard for the country. Now is a time when the country is in trouble. I am deeply afraid of falling short of my responsibilities, as I am of meager virtue and scarce ability, burdened with heavy responsibilities. However, in handling all affairs, I have acted on the instructions of the central government and strived to take the four matters of the country, the people, the facts, and the suppression of communism as prerequisites. First, take the country as a prerequisite, because the country is formed by the concerted efforts of everyone. The strength of a country does not lie in having many soldiers, but in having strong people. Therefore, the first thing to do is to support righteousness to encourage the people's hearts, so that everyone can fulfill their responsibilities, be loyal to the country, and be loyal to the nation, eliminate selfish views, and seek the permanent welfare of the country. Second, take the people as a prerequisite, that is, to relieve the people's suffering, eliminate corruption, suppress bandits, and abolish excessive and miscellaneous taxes. In the past year, we have continuously eliminated corruption. However, whether we have completely eliminated it is also related to politics. I believe that we can definitely go down this road. The bandits are also gradually being suppressed. Although we cannot leave our doors unlocked at night, we can still walk safely. We have tried our best to abolish excessive and miscellaneous taxes, and the main goal is to enable the people to live and work in peace. Third, take the facts as a prerequisite. I have always advocated telling the truth and doing practical things, striving for self-improvement, and overthrowing the mentality of dependence, doubt, and hypocrisy. I personally believe that the Chinese people all have patriotic ideas and are not bad people. Therefore, we should eliminate the above points, seek truth from facts, and strive to benefit the country and the nation, and walk together on one road to achieve the goal of saving the country. Fourth, take the suppression of communism as a prerequisite. The fallacies of communism confuse the world and are completely incompatible with the national conditions. In recent years, communist bandits have rioted, and their brutality exceeds that of bandits. If we want to save the country, we must first eliminate communism. We will never allow it to exist within the borders of Hebei and Chahar and will thoroughly eliminate it. The above four are the facts of the past and will also be the direction of the future. The press is a guiding organ of society. The development of the press is related to the enlightenment of the people, the improvement of society, the promotion of national policies, and the support of the public. It is hoped that you in the press will fulfill your social responsibilities, promote the historical mission, and not hesitate to give me guidance, deeply understand the difficulties of the times, and jointly maintain the overall situation. I am greatly honored." (10th)

Grain Prices in Northern Anhui Remain Surprisingly High; Have Not Eased Due to Prolonged Drought; Disaster Has Taken Shape in Various Counties 72

Bengbu Correspondence, Since the end of October, due to drought and lack of rain in northern Anhui, tense situation, and scarce sources of miscellaneous grains, grain prices have risen step by step. The Bengbu authorities initially planned to suppress them and limit further rises. However, the established situation was impossible to reverse. Before long, the Anhui Provincial Government prohibited the export of food grains as a restrictive measure. However, with food grains unable to circulate freely, the grain market was virtually stagnant, and grain prices remained stiff. Although the central government subsequently implemented food grain regulation and prohibited restrictions on exports in order to balance supply and demand and provide relief, grain prices in northern Anhui remained firm due to the prolonged drought for a month and have not fallen back yet. There was light rain like silk on the 10th of this month, but the fields could not be thoroughly soaked. The market price of river bottom soybeans and wheat has not eased at all. The export of soybeans is surging, and flour mills are buying wheat as much as possible. The prices of various grains still have an upward trend. The recent market prices in Bengbu are: good quality Hehua wheat, 18 yuan; Shouzhou red wheat, 17 yuan 8 jiao 9; soybeans, 14 yuan 7 jiao 5 fen; high-grade rice, 18 yuan (the above are calculated per shi); and the price of first-class flour has risen to 4 yuan 3 jiao per bag. Families below the middle class, seeing the high cost of rice and firewood and the surprising prices of everything, are all complaining bitterly, feeling that their livelihoods are difficult. Moreover, disaster victims in various counties are forming groups to flee the famine. At this time of winter cold and drought, with the sowing of wheat overdue, a disaster has taken shape. The winter famine is more serious than the spring famine, which is truly worthy of attention. (11th)

Kunshan: Sent to Shanghai to Apprehend Local Bandits 73

The home of Zou Meiting, a farmer in Anqiao Village, the second district of the county, was suddenly robbed by bandits on the night of the 22nd of last month. Before leaving, they also kidnapped his second son, Fucheng. It was not until the day before yesterday that they received a letter from the bandits, stating the method and path of the gambling tickets. Zou immediately submitted the original letter to the Public Security Bureau. Director Dong immediately dispatched Detective Li of the Detective Squad, leading detective police and the victim, disguised, to Shanghai on the afternoon of the 8th of this month. According to the designated address, they joined forces with patrolmen and arrested four bandits. During interrogation, they confessed that the hostage was hidden in Yaoshan Township, Changshu. Detective Li then joined forces with Shanghai Public Security Bureau detectives and rushed to Changshu overnight, recovered the hostage, and arrested two bandits guarding the hostage, and brought them back to Shanghai. They confessed their names as Xie Changlin, Shi Xin-gen, Wang Xiulong, Min Chen, Duan Mingchen, and Yang Jinyuan, etc. The Kunshan County Public Security Bureau dispatched personnel to Shanghai on the 11th to escort the bandits and hostage back to the county for interrogation.

Suzhou: Frequent Reports of Robberies in Urban and Rural Areas 74

Since the beginning of winter, there have been frequent reports of robberies in urban and rural areas. A robbery also occurred in Xiangcheng Township the day before yesterday, with the homes of Xu Jiayu and Xu Buchang being robbed, as well as a bird gun. Moreover, the Hengchangxiang, Laidetang, Yongchunxiang, Wu Bomao, Zhao Xiemao, Zhengfengxiang, and eight other shops in Nijiawan Town, Huangdai Township, were robbed. Wang A-gen, Xue Qiuting, and Wang Jiayu were injured and six guns were taken from the head of the security corps. After robbing for about two hours, they escaped. The Huangdai Township Public Security Sub-bureau and Security Corps immediately dispatched teams to pursue the robbers, but were unsuccessful. County Magistrate Deng, upon receiving the report, ordered the Public Security Bureau and Security Corps on the 12th to dispatch teams separately to strictly investigate and punish the stolen goods and robbers. He also reported to the Winter Defense Committee, as well as the Second District of the Water Police. District Chief Zhou immediately dispatched warships to patrol Yangcheng Lake and other places to prevent bandits from fleeing to various villages. Director Song of the Winter Defense Office heard that he would implement the dispatch of teams to encircle and suppress bandits to maintain local security.

Various Goods Expensive in Suzhou 75

Recently, Suzhou has experienced a continuous shortage of rice and wheat, leading to gradual price increases. In just a few days, the price of rice has risen by more than one yuan, and the price of wheat has also risen by six or seven jiao. Because of this, various snacks that are necessary for common people, such as sliced noodles, sesame cakes, and fried dough sticks, have all been raised in price uniformly to maintain their capital. The general poor people are all complaining bitterly.

Chamber of Commerce Sends Personnel to Solicit Aircraft Donation 76

The Wuxian County Chamber of Commerce was ordered to raise funds for aircraft donation, with a target of 30,000 yuan. Merchants from various industries have separately raised more than 11,000 yuan, all of which have been sent to the province. The Second District Commissioner's Office, considering that the amount of donations raised in this county was still significantly insufficient, specially sent Zhang Zhongyu to Suzhou to supervise the collection. After arriving in Suzhou, Committee Member Zhang immediately consulted with County Magistrate Deng and Cheng Ganqing, Chairman of the County Chamber of Commerce, several times. In addition to having the Chamber of Commerce issue a letter urging various industries to quickly raise and submit the funds, on the 12th, Zhang Haishan and Xu Woyun, along with police officers dispatched by the police station, set off for Jingde Road, Guanqian Street, the East-West-Central Market, Yuyuxiang, and other places to solicit donations from each store that had not yet paid the donation, in order to gather the amount and remit it.

Fundraising Efforts for Suiyuan from All Sectors 77

Various sectors in Wuxian County are working diligently to raise funds to aid Suiyuan. They have already raised over 10,000 yuan. The Wuping Music Troupe of the New Suzhou Club held a musical performance yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM to raise funds. County Magistrate Deng's special envoy presided over the opening ceremony. The Wuxian Women's Aid Suiyuan Association has raised 2,000 yuan and purchased cloth, silk, and cotton. These materials will be distributed to various girls' schools for making vests to be sent to the front lines. The association will also hold a variety show to raise funds for Suiyuan.

Wuxi: Reporting Arson Attempt for Insurance Claim 78

The Baohe Tang Traditional Chinese Medicine store on Tonghui Road near Huinong Bridge in our county, owned by Xu Baofa, caught fire unexpectedly last month, causing significant damage to neighboring properties. However, since Wu had fire insurance, there is suspicion of arson to claim insurance. Recently, Xu agreed to pay his neighbor Shao Er'er 50 yuan after receiving the insurance money and donate 100 yuan to the fire brigade. This matter came to the attention of Yu Zhuo'an, the town head of Huiqin Town, and Qiao Houfu, the head of the fifth bao, who reported it. Yesterday, they convened an emergency meeting of the baojia and decided to jointly petition the local court's prosecutor's office to investigate the matter according to law.

One Day's Contribution to the Nation 79

The One Day's Contribution to the Nation Promotion Committee in our county held a meeting at the county party headquarters yesterday. Chairman Li Tiping reported that since the initiative was launched in our county, all sectors have enthusiastically supported it. As of the 10th, 15,183 yuan and 16 cents have been donated. The following matters were resolved: (1) Revised and approved the organization's constitution. (2) Encouraged all households that have not yet donated to contribute enthusiastically. (3) Decided to remit 10,000 yuan to the front lines first. The destination will be telegraphed to Commander Chiang's headquarters in Luoyang for instructions. Furthermore, the silk factory's labor union in our county purchased and manufactured 1,000 silk cotton vests to be sent to Suiyuan to comfort the soldiers.

Wujiang: Committee Member Oversees Collection of Aircraft Donation 80

Our county's chamber of commerce was previously ordered by the provincial government to raise 6,250 yuan for an aircraft donation to celebrate a birthday. However, the business in our county is too sluggish, and only 1,704 yuan has been raised, far short of the assigned amount. Yesterday, Zhang Buyu, a commissioner from the Second District Commissioner's Office, was dispatched to the county to oversee the collection. Our county's chamber of commerce remitted another 500 yuan. For the outstanding amount, Zhang ordered the chamber of commerce to clear the entire amount before the 15th of this month.

Nantong: Drug Dealer Executed 81

The Fourth District Security Command of Jiangsu Province arrested Shen Keiren, a drug dealer from Liuqiao. After trial, he was sentenced to death. Commander Ge received an order from the Military Commission on the 11th, stating that Shen Keiren had previously been sentenced to imprisonment by the Nantong Local Court for selling opium substitutes. After serving his term and being released from prison, he resumed selling drugs. The evidence was conclusive. The original sentence of death according to law was deemed appropriate and was to be carried out. At around 11:00 AM, he was tied up and taken to the execution ground in the east of the city and shot.

Zhenjiang: Large-Scale Vehicle Inspection 82

The Jiangsu Provincial Highway Administration, recognizing that the sturdiness of long-distance buses is crucial to the safety of passengers, is conducting thorough inspections of long-distance buses as a matter of prudence, and any that are found to be damaged or substandard will be eliminated. It is understood that the administration recently conducted an inspection on the Su-Xi Road, which has now been completed. The results are satisfactory. It is reported that the administration will conduct another large-scale inspection within this month to identify the superior and inferior vehicles and ensure passenger safety.

Yangzhou: Long-Awaited Rain Nourishes Wheat Fields 83

The four districts surrounding Yangzhou city have suffered from a severe autumn and winter drought. In areas where wheat was planted by laboriously drawing water, most of the seeds did not sprout. Those that did sprout are withering due to the lack of rain and snow. Farmers have been longing for rain for ages. Fortunately, light rain began on the evening of the 10th, turning heavier at 10:00 PM and continuing throughout the night. On the 11th, it rained intermittently, becoming heavy again in the evening. The total rainfall is estimated to be about three inches. The wheat seedlings that have sprouted can be expected to recover. However, it is difficult to predict whether the seeds that have not yet sprouted will be able to do so.

Education Bureau Deducts Salaries to Aid Suiyuan 84

The Education Bureau of our county, recognizing the efforts of the Suiyuan soldiers in resisting bandits and puppets, proposed that one day's salary from all primary schools under the bureau's jurisdiction be donated to the front lines. A total of 123 yuan and 62 cents was deducted and has now been handed over to the Central Bank for remittance.

Dangtu: Construction of Dangbo Road Begins 85

The county government, in order to construct the Dangbo Highway, ordered the districts and bao to conscript laborers, specifying that men aged 18 to 45 were eligible. The road will run from the county seat through Xizhen, Danyang, Xinshi, to Bowang, and end at Erlang Temple in Lishui, Jiangsu. The section from the county seat to Bowang is 80 li long and is scheduled to begin construction on December 10th and be completed in two months. The road surface is specified to be 7.5 meters wide, with a minimum of 6.5 meters, and the height must exceed the highest water level by 6 centimeters. If any bao laborer is late for work by one day, they will be fined one day's labor.

Yuyao: Strict Crackdown on Private Salt 86

The Liangzhe Salt Transportation Office stated that the coastal counties of Zhejiang have historically been salt-producing areas. However, in recent years, salt production has not decreased, but tax revenue has declined. The reason is that illegally produced salt is rampant, which must be strictly investigated to increase tax revenue. In addition to instructing the salt affairs tax police to diligently investigate, the office also ordered the county magistrates to assist at any time and strictly prohibit illegal trafficking, illegal production, illegal transportation, and illegal sale. At the same time, model salt shops should be established in busy city areas.

Ningbo: Fenghua and Cixi Forbid Rice Exports 87

The governments of Fenghua and Cixi counties stated that the statistics of food production and sales this year are still insufficient to meet local needs. However, some unscrupulous merchants are still privately transporting rice out of the area from time to time, causing prices to soar. To maintain the people's livelihood and balance grain prices, rice merchants are prohibited from transporting rice out of the area any further. Once discovered, the rice will be confiscated, and the merchant will be ordered to suspend business operations.

Jiangtian Steamer Shipwreck Dispute 88

The New Jiangtian Steamer, which operates between Shanghai and Ningbo, damaged three barges docked at the pier on the 9th while sailing from [blank] to Ningbo due to negligence. Afterwards, the civilian ship crew union made verbal representations, but no results were achieved due to the great distance between the two sides. The union, fearing that it would incite public anger among the crew and further escalate the dispute, has sent a letter to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to negotiate compensation.

Tax Police Shoot Fisherman 89

Wang Xingchang, a resident of Songlin Township in Fenghua, who earns a living by fishing, was working at sea the other day when he passed through the waters of Xianghe Tan and was suddenly accosted by several tax police stationed there, who demanded fish. Because he had no fish to give them, he was shot and killed. Afterwards, his family reported the incident and requested that the culprits be apprehended. The deceased's family is in dire straits, and the local people are indignant.

Hangzhou: Partial Demolition and Reconstruction of Hangzhou Seawall 90

The Zhejiang Construction Department stated that the stone seawalls of the Shuo, Gan, Wu, and Ding numbered dikes near the Babao area of the Hangping section were found to be leaning outwards, and the situation was very dangerous. After obtaining approval from the provincial government to allocate funds for repairs, Zhou Zhenlun, director of the Water Conservancy Engineering Office, and technician Xu Yunqing were sent by car to Haining to conduct a detailed survey yesterday. It was decided to fundamentally renovate the dangerous sections of the dike and rebuild them to ensure the safety of the dike bank.

Local News

14 Million Yuan Loan Agreement for Jing-Gan Railway Signed Yesterday; Interest at 9 Li Per Month, Repaid in 20 Installments Over 10 Years; Payment Method Stipulated, Jin Cheng as General Representative 91

The Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Railways have signed a contract to extend the railway from Xuancheng to Guixi and issue 14 million yuan in Jing-Gan Railway construction bonds, which will be issued next New Year's Day. Railway Director Zhang Gongquan has borrowed the full amount from eight banks, including the Bank of Communications, etc., and the Four Banks Savings Association. The lending banks have formed a syndicate, designating Jin Cheng Bank as the general representative. After the contract was drafted, it was signed in Shanghai the day before yesterday by Tang Shoumin of the Bank of Communications, Zhu Runsheng of the Agricultural Bank of China, Zhou Zuomin of Jin Cheng Bank, Ye Fuxiao of Dalu Bank, Wang Shaoxian of the Yanye Bank, Hu Bijiang of the Zhongnan Bank, Qian Xinzhi of the Four Banks Savings Association, and Xu Xinliu of the Zhejiang Industrial Bank. Zhou Zuomin, general manager of Jin Cheng Bank and general representative of the syndicate, took it to Beijing that evening. Yesterday, it was signed by Zhang Gongquan, Minister of Railways. A reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency obtained the original text of the contract, which is as follows: Article 1: The total amount of this loan is 14 million yuan in national currency, which is exclusively for the construction of the Xuan-Gui section of the railway and its equipment. This loan includes 4 million yuan borrowed from the Bank of Communications, 3 million yuan borrowed from the Agricultural Bank of China, 2 million yuan borrowed from the Jin Cheng Bank, 1 million yuan borrowed from the Four Banks Savings Association, 500,000 yuan from the Trust Department, 1 million yuan borrowed from the Dalu Bank, 1 million yuan borrowed from the Zhongnan Bank, 1 million yuan borrowed from the Yanye Bank, and 500,000 yuan borrowed from the Zhejiang Industrial Bank. Article 2: This loan will be paid in five installments: 3 million yuan will be paid on the date of signing the contract, and 3 million yuan will be paid in January, April, and July of the 26th year of the Republic of China, respectively. 2 million yuan will be paid in September. Each bank shall make the payment on schedule in accordance with the borrowing ratio specified in the preceding article. Article 3: The interest rate on this loan is 9 li per month, calculated from the date of each payment. Starting from the 26th year of the Republic of China, it will be repaid in 20 installments over 10 years. Principal and interest will be paid once every June and December, and the amount will be in accordance with the regulations for repayment of principal and interest. The table is attached as part of this contract. Article 4: After the signing of this contract, the Ministry of Railways shall provide Jing-Gan Railway construction bonds with a face value of 14 million yuan, which will be received by the syndicate as collateral for the principal and interest of this loan. The aforementioned bonds are set at an annual interest rate of 6 li, with principal and interest repaid once every June and December. Before the bonds are issued, the Ministry of Railways shall issue preliminary bonds for the syndicate to receive. After the bonds are issued and allocated, the syndicate shall return the preliminary bonds to the Ministry of Railways for cancellation. Article 5: In order to ensure the repayment of principal and interest on the Anglo-Chinese Boxer Indemnity loan used for the Yue-Han Railway, the Ministry of Railways, with the approval of the Board of Directors, shall provide a special fund of 6.2 million yuan in national currency each year from the 26th year of the Republic of China to the 35th year of the Republic of China for the repayment of Boxer Indemnity principal and interest (details in the general contract). According to the provisions of the Yue-Han Railway's Anglo-Chinese Boxer Indemnity loan agreement, the principal repaid in each installment, excluding interest, will still be transferred by the Ministry of Railways together with the remaining balance of the aforementioned special fund and designated as the fund for repayment of principal and interest on the Jing-Gan Railway construction bonds and various loans. Article 6: In order to ensure the repayment of principal and interest on the Jing-Gan Railway construction bonds and various loans, in addition to designating the funds specified in the preceding article as the fund, the Ministry of Railways shall provide 2 million yuan in national currency each year from the operating income of the Xuan-Gui section from the 28th year of the Republic of China to the 35th year of the Republic of China and add it to the fund. The upper construction bonds and various loans for the Xuan-Gui section shall be repaid for principal and interest. Article 7: The syndicate agrees that it has the priority to withdraw interest on the 450,000 pounds borrowed by the Board of Directors from the Xuan-Gui section for materials, as well as the price of 450,000 pounds for materials purchased by the factory on credit. Article 8: The custody and management of the Jing-Gan Railway construction bond fund and various loan funds shall be handled by a fund custody committee jointly organized by one representative each from the Ministry of Finance and the Auditing Department, two representatives designated by the Ministry of Railways, two representatives recommended by the Board of Directors and the syndicate, and one representative recommended by the manufacturer. The fund shall not be used without the resolution and issuance of checks by the committee. Article 9: The principal and interest receivable on the Jing-Gan Railway construction bonds shall be received by the syndicate as part of the principal and interest due on this loan. The shortfall shall be supplemented in full by the Fund Custody Committee in accordance with the provisions of the principal and interest repayment schedule for this loan. After receiving the principal and interest on the bonds, the syndicate shall submit the bond interest tickets to the Fund Custody Committee for submission to the Ministry of Railways for destruction. Article 18: The Ministry of Railways shall purchase materials from manufacturers on credit, up to 450,000 pounds sterling, with a weekly interest rate of 6 li. Interest only shall be paid before the 28th year of the Republic of China, and principal shall be repaid starting from the 28th year of the Republic of China in 16 installments over eight years. All contracts and loan agreements for the purchase of materials shall be copied separately by the Ministry of Railways and sent to the syndicate and the Fund Custody Committee for record. Article 11: In addition to this loan and the materials purchased on credit by the Board of Directors and manufacturers, the budget for domestic labor and materials for the Xuan-Gui construction project still requires 10 million yuan in national currency. If there is any interest-bearing loan in the future, all road assets and operating income of the section, excluding the 2 million yuan mentioned in Article 6, shall be used as parallel collateral for the various loans opened in this article. Before the various loans are repaid, there shall be no further mortgages or sales. Article 12: Regarding revenue and expenditure accounting matters, before the loan is repaid, the Board of Directors shall recommend a head of the accounting department, and the syndicate shall recommend a deputy head of the accounting department and head of the cashier's department. The Ministry of Railways shall present the appointments to the Chief Comptroller for approval. Regarding audit matters, the syndicate shall recommend a chief auditor, and the Board of Directors shall recommend a deputy chief auditor. Article 13: In addition to allocating the principal and interest repaid by the Ministry of Railways to the Anglo-Chinese Boxer Indemnity loan used for the Yue-Han Railway as a fund in accordance with the provisions of Article 5 of this contract, the Board of Directors shall not be responsible for any other repayments. Article 14: This contract is drafted in nine copies, one each for the Bank of Communications, Jin Cheng Bank, Dalu Bank, Zhongnan Bank, Agricultural Bank of China, Four Banks Savings Association, Yanye Bank, Zhejiang Industrial Bank, and the Ministry of Railways. It shall be cancelled jointly on the date of full repayment of the principal and interest of the loan. (Attached table omitted)

Cai Yuanpei's Condition Improved Yesterday 96

After the Suiyuan border situation became critical, overseas Chinese were extremely concerned. Li has already returned to Shanghai. It is said that since the recapture of Bailingmiao in northern Suiyuan, the bandits have lost their fighting spirit. Wang Ying was originally the son of Wang Tongchun, a major landlord in Hetao. Most of his troops were workers who had cultivated the land in those years, so the move to return to allegiance was natural. At present, bandit puppet troops are gathered in Shangdu. If they do not counterattack, the Suiyuan affair can be considered to have come to an end for a period of time. Song Zheyuan's attitude is very much watched by the whole country. Song is very chivalrous and has a very strong sense of national concept. All of his 29th Army are patriotic men of zeal and are filled with righteous indignation and have a good attitude. They are very submissive to the central government. Song's environment is special and difficult to deal with. However, since the establishment of the Hebei-Chahar Political Council, although under threat, no treaties have been signed, etc.

Tian Bo Lie Lectured Yesterday on International Situation and the League of Nations, Visited New Buildings in the City in the Morning, Then Visited President Cai's Illness, Scheduled to Return to England by Boat at 8:30 Tomorrow Morning 100

Tian Bo Lie, President of the International Historical Society, accompanied by Kang Xuanyi and Jiang Jianbai, visited new buildings such as the Municipal Hospital, Library, and Museum in the city center yesterday morning. He then visited Mr. Cai Yuanpei, President of the Academia Sinica, and gave a public lecture at the YMCA at 4:30 PM. This afternoon, St. John's University held a tea party to entertain Mr. Tian. It is reported that Mr. Tian is scheduled to return to England by the Changxing Company's Asia Queen at 8:30 tomorrow morning. The following is an excerpt from Mr. Tian's speech at the YMCA yesterday. First, He Bingsong delivered an introductory speech. After the speech, Mr. Tian stood up and spoke on "The International Situation and the League of Nations." He first described the international trends after the European War, and then said the diplomatic relations between Britain and the international community, according to Balfour (League of Nations advisor in 1921) said that the emergence of the League of Nations, for diplomacy to resolve international disputes a new discovery. As a result, international diplomacy is divided into two new and old ways, but because we promote the new diplomacy too fast, before the new diplomacy has proved its value, we have given up the old law, now we are all in this difficulty in receiving efficiency. In the current Italian-Abyssinian incident, the judgments of 52 countries are ineffective. Although A'er still sends representatives in the League of Nations, it is impossible to say that it is an independent country. Both new and old diplomacy have tended to fail. We should combine the new and old diplomacy to build a new political system. Former British Foreign Secretary Canning said that public opinion and propaganda had a lot of power in the old diplomatic policy. After Canning's death, Palmerston succeeded as Foreign Secretary and adopted his policy, which made British diplomacy successful for more than 30 years. In 1864, he was defeated by Bismarck of Germany, and the new diplomatic policy was born in response to the facts. Empty words are no match for weapons, and morality is no match for force. England was humiliated by Prussia, just as the League of Nations was humiliated by Italy. England only recognized the independence of Belgium in the past, so Germany committed the territory of Belgium during the European War, but now Germany knows that England will protect Belgium and will never dare to invade it again. Article 4 of the International Treaty, the Kellogg-Briand Pact, and the Locarno Treaty are all clauses expressing peaceful resolution of disputes. But how is the actual performance? Now I hope that there will be genuine legal control among nations. We are willing to transform the League of Nations and Article 4 of the League of Nations to further consolidate the territorial integrity of member states. It is ineffective if we invite aggressive countries to discuss everything together and transform it in this way. King Edward VIII of England said that we should sincerely support the League of Nations to resolve all disputes, but the lessons of the facts show that British diplomats will never adopt this. The League of Nations can still exist now, because there are still many countries behind the League of Nations that support the League of Nations, so the League of Nations is still an inviolable organization. Past lessons believe that it cannot be destroyed any more. The League of Nations is not dead and needs to continue to exist. The greater the lessons learned, the deeper the understanding of the international community. The past work of the League of Nations, such as public health, charitable organizations, and statistical surveys, are all beneficial undertakings for the world, and the International Court of Justice is also a pioneering initiative for the world to uphold justice. We are born in the political world and should engage in political activities and support political progress. China has always expressed faith in the League of Nations, and although past facts are not satisfactory, I hope it will not be distracted. We can represent unrealistic idealism with realism.

German Military Officer Major Xi Shao Zuo Died Yesterday 102

Major Himmel Senni G, a German military advisor to the Central Government, died in Shanghai at 4:00 AM yesterday. Mr. Xi came to Shanghai from Suzhou this week for a short trip and stayed at a friend's residence at 133 Shanzhong Road. Unexpectedly, he suddenly contracted malaria and died despite medical treatment. Mr. Xi has been serving as a military advisor in China for three and a half years. He first worked in Nanjing and was transferred to Suzhou last year. Mr. Xi was born in Neitz, Germany in January 1891. His wife and two children are currently in Shanghai. The cremation is scheduled to take place at 3:00 PM next Monday at the church of the International Funeral Parlor on Jiaozhou Road.

Suspension of Hunan Rice Transport to Guangdong, Suspension of Syndicated Loans 104

After the opening of the Yuehan Railway, the transport and sale of Hunan rice to Guangdong was carried out smoothly under the joint leadership of the Shanghai Syndicate, the Hunan Rice Merchants Association, and the provincial governments of Hunan and Guangdong. Recently, Hunan rice merchants took advantage of the large amount of sales rights to manipulate prices, which aroused the resentment of Guangdong distributors. As a result, rice prices fluctuated and citizens complained. In addition, the Yuehan Railway could not transport according to the stipulated time, and there were also cases of supply and demand not meeting. As a result, the transport of Hunan rice to Guangdong was suddenly suspended. China, Jiaotong, and other banks in this city had planned to use 10 million to 50 million yuan in funds to handle the syndicated loan for the transport and sale of national rice. It was decided that the transport of Hunan rice to Guangdong would be the first step. Now that the transport of Hunan rice to Guangdong has been suspended, the progress of the syndicate is facing many difficulties and has been temporarily suspended. Each bank will continue to handle it on its own. A reporter from Xinxin News Agency learned from banking circles yesterday that the suspension of Hunan rice transport to Guangdong should be rescued as soon as possible and restored as soon as possible. Otherwise, foreign rice will take the opportunity to invade, and the rice trade of more than 20 million yuan in Guangdong Province may still be plundered by foreign merchants. It is reported that the Bank of Communications has sent Li Zhongzhi to Hunan to investigate the truth and will meet with Yu Jichuan, Director of the Hunan Provincial Department of Construction, to discuss the matter.

Women's Relief Association Tea Party to Entertain Women Tomorrow, 4:00 PM on the 14th at the International Hotel, Discuss Relief Matters as Resolved by the Board of Directors 105

Wang Xiaoying, Liu Wang Liming, Tu Kunfan, Wang Ruizhu, Jin Guangmei, Bao Zhining, Wu Caiyi, Tang Guanyu, Lin Kecong (Huang acting), Xian Wu Wenhua, Huang Bingpei, Bu Zhenhua, Zhang Quanping (Huang Bingpei acting), Xie Zuyi, Yan Yaqing (Xie acting), Cai Renbao's wife, Li Xiaofeng, Lu Mingzhi of Nanyang Girls' High School, Jin Yuhua of Daozhong Girls' High School, Wang Xiakun of Minli Girls' High School, Li Xiyong of Peiming Girls' High School, Hu Lan of Wuben Girls' High School, Huang Zhuqiu of the Chinese Women's Life Improvement Society, and others attended, presided over by Wang Xiaoying, with Lin Wen recording. The details are recorded as follows:
