The Contractor for Labor at the China Merchants Bureau's South Wharf Has Been Replaced by the Bureau Because of Insufficient Labor and Delay in Ship Schedules 106

The state-run China Merchants Bureau recently removed Li Huanxin, the contractor for labor at the South Wharf, for poor management and violation of the contract for labor. After repeated warnings, he remained indifferent. The contracting right of Li Huanxin was revoked, and Qiu Dinglai, the original alternate bidder, was assigned to take over the labor affairs of the South Wharf. A responsible person from the bureau issued a statement saying that the bid for labor at the South Wharf of the bureau was submitted on August 20 of this year, and the bids were opened on the same day. On August 24 of the same month, the bid review meeting reviewed the bids and selected Li Huanxin as the winning bidder, and Qiu Dinglai as the alternate winning bidder. The bureau ordered Li Huanxin to come to the bureau on September 2 of this year to sign the contract for contracting the labor at the South Wharf, and ordered the wharf management office to report that the contractor officially took over the labor and transportation affairs of the South Wharf on the morning of September 16 of this year. Afterwards, internal disputes occurred within the contractor, involving a large number of people. Although it had no direct relationship with the bureau's business, it could have been ignored. However, newspapers published notices one after another, which was not a good thing. The bureau is still investigating the truth of the case. However, since the contractor took over, he has been poorly managed, his measures have been flawed, and there is insufficient labor. Moreover, the bureau has repeatedly reported that there are cases of deducting wages, and the new laborers he uses are weak and inefficient, resulting in slow loading and unloading and delays in ship schedules. He has also made things difficult for customers, arbitrarily demanding money, and customers have made many complaints. According to reports, the contractor has also made things difficult for customs brokers. After reviewing the circumstances, it has violated the provisions of the contracting contract. The bureau has repeatedly ordered the wharf management office to give earnest warnings and limited the contractor to thoroughly improve the situation within a certain period of time, so that all bad measures can be eliminated and the schedules of each ship will not be delayed. Originally, it was hoped to give him a final opportunity to revitalize, but the contractor remained indifferent within the time limit and did not have any rectification measures. Moreover, within the time limit, the cargo transportation work of the Taishun ship could not be handled quickly, resulting in the ship's schedule being delayed as before. The bureau has repeatedly warned him, but he does not know how to repent. If it is not strictly rectified, how can we maintain business and value customer trust? Therefore, the bureau ordered the contractor Li Huanxin to have his contracting right revoked in accordance with the joint regulations, and ordered the original alternate bidder Qiu Dinglai to come to the bureau to pay the deposit and prepare a reliable shop guarantee to sign the contracting contract, and to take over the labor affairs of the South Wharf on a fixed date. The bureau also ordered the wharf management office to transfer the order to its subordinates, and to give the new contractor as much convenience as possible under the principle of increasing the efficiency of the bureau's business. Before the new contractor Qiu Dinglai takes over, the original contractor Li Huanxin is still ordered to be fully responsible for all labor work at the South Wharf. The bureau will hold the contractor accountable for any losses incurred. In order to take into account the interests of customers and the livelihood of workers, the bureau has also made additional regulations when signing the contract for contracting labor with the new contractor. The contractor shall not reduce the wages paid to workers after contracting compared with before September of this year (ie, before the implementation of the bidding), and shall not increase the additional labor force that customers are willing to pay compared with before September of this year, in order to achieve the purpose of eliminating malpractices such as deducting wages and extorting and making things difficult.

Labor Service Propaganda Held in Gaohang Yesterday 107

Yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM, the Shanghai Labor Service Committee convened a discussion meeting with representatives from all sectors of the Gaohang Township in Pudong at the Municipal Committee Office. The purpose was to discuss propaganda matters. More than 70 people attended, including the district director Pan Hongding, Donggou Police Chief Wang Chongshan, Gaohang District Farmers' Association Zhu Runsheng, Shen Baotian, and various school principals such as Ling Songjiao.

Chairman Hongding began with a report, stating that the purpose of Shanghai's ordered implementation of labor service is to enable everyone to serve the country, to develop construction projects, and to cultivate a habit of labor and a spirit of service. The projects undertaken by the district's labor service include dredging and protecting the Tanghe River, Henghang River, Zhuangshupu River, and Xiantangwan River, all of which are of great benefit to water conservancy and transportation. Now that service is about to begin, it is feared that some sectors are still unclear about the meaning and methods of labor service, and it is hoped that everyone will make efforts to publicize it.

Next, Yu Hui, a representative from the Labor Service Committee, reported on service methods and gave instructions on propaganda guidelines. It was decided that (1) starting immediately, all schools and Bao'an Tuan (local security corps) in the district would be fully mobilized to go to the villages for propaganda; (2) preparations would be made for a commencement ceremony, and meaningful entertainment would be included to encourage farmers' interest in service. The meeting then discussed various issues related to the engineering aspect and adjourned.

Comfort Money Donated By The Wei Tong Factory Employees to Aid Suiyuan 110

The Weitong Textile Factory workers' aid-Sui donation initiators, Wang Zhengping, Zhang Xilin, Jiang Minyu, etc., stated in a letter that "At this time of bandit invasion of Sui, and the critical moment of survival, we workers are also a part of the nation and naturally bear the important responsibility of saving the nation, and should also fulfill the obligation of rear support and comfort. Therefore, in addition to the one-day wage movement already conducted by the factory, we have specially joined forces with our comrades to initiate saving pocket money to慰勞慰勞 the soldiers on the front lines. Now we send the donations from colleagues in the machine repair section, totaling 44.08 yuan, to your newspaper office for transfer, and hope that workers in all factories will not shirk their responsibility and implement it uniformly."

Zhengtai Factory Employees Continue to Donate A Large Sum to Aid Suiyuan 111

At the beginning of the Suiyuan War, the owner of the Zhengtai Xinyi Rubber Factory in this port, realizing that the soldiers fighting bloody battles on the front lines were in urgent need of supplies, generously donated 2,000 pairs of the factory's famous "Huilipai" rubber shoes, and entrusted them to the Shen Bao for transfer to the Suiyuan Pacification Commissioner's Office in Sui Province. Yesterday, General Fu's letter of thanks and receipt were received. The value of these rubber shoes, just the shipping cost alone, has reached 216 yuan, totaling over 2,000 yuan. Now, all the employees of the factory have again donated 523.5 yuan from one day's wages and saved meal expenses (totaling 739.5 yuan including shipping costs), still entrusting it to the Shen Bao for transfer to the front. Furthermore, the factory had previously had a dispute with the Shiye Rubber Factory over the name "Wanli Shoes." It was reasonable to pursue compensation for the loss from the Shiye Factory, but the factory, considering the national crisis and the relationship between fellow businesses and intermediaries, could not bear to be harsh. Therefore, they requested the owner of the Shiye Factory to generously donate 200 yuan in national currency for the purpose of aiding Suiyuan. The patriotism and benevolent actions of the company are worthy of emulation.

Charity Organization Relief Association Held Design Committee Meeting Yesterday 112

The Design Expert Committee of the Shanghai Charity Organization Joint Relief Association held its first committee meeting at the Eight Immortals Bridge YMCA at 4:00 PM yesterday. More than 20 people attended, including Qu Wenliu, Huang Hanzhi, Guan Jiongzhi, Feng Yangshan, Zhao Jinqing, Chen Tiesheng, Liu Wenlin, Wang Zhenchang, Li Zhu, Pan Tang Guanyu, and the wives of Niu Huisheng and Mei Huaquan. Qu Wenliu and Niu Huisheng's wife chaired the meeting. The chairman first reported the purpose of the meeting and the situation in the war zone, and then discussed the following proposals:

(1) Proposal to raise supplies: It was resolved:

(A) Clothing: (1) Women's inner and outer cotton-flannel clothes, gloves, hats, shoes, socks, and bedding, etc.; (2) Children's (from infants to 15 years old) inner and outer cotton-flannel clothes, gloves, shoes, hats, socks, and bedding, etc. Note: All of the above items must be clean and tidy. Damaged items must be repaired.

(B) Food: (1) Various canned meats and vegetables, or prepared snacks, pastries, milk powder, etc.; (2) Rice and flour; (3) Other foods. Note: The most important thing is that all of the above foods must be fresh.

(C) Medicines

(2) Proposal for fundraising methods: It was resolved:

(A) Official propaganda: (1) Publish this plan in newspapers; (2) Broadcast announcements on the radio; (3) Distribute announcements door-to-door, and request the assistance of the post office;

(B) Each street in the Shanghai Chinese Concession should be used as a fundraising unit;

(C) Fundraisers must wear badges issued by this association to show their seriousness.

(3) Proposal for fundraising areas: It was resolved that the city should be divided into eight districts, with the association as the general fundraising site: (1) Pudong District (Pudong Commune); (2) Puxi District (Puxi Commune); (3) Zhabei District (Zhabei People's Needlework Institute); (4) City Center District (Social Affairs Bureau); (5) Nanshi District (Public Education Center); (6) French Concession District (Eight Immortals Bridge YMCA); (7) Public Concession District (this association); (8) Lingdong District (Pudong YMCA).

(4) Proposal for fundraising dates: It was resolved that a general fundraising campaign would be held, and the dates would be determined by the committee.

Central Mint Review Committee Passes New Currency Out of Factory 113

The review committee of the Central Mint held its 18th regular meeting at the Central Bank at 4:30 PM on the afternoon of the 11th of this month. Chairman Kong was unable to attend due to illness, and Committee Member Chen Jian'an acted as chairman. Committee members Ye Zhuotang, Song Hanzhang, Xu Xinliu, Ye Fuxiao, Xi Demao, Shao Yanshan, Lu Zhuqing, Ma Xier, Geng Aide, Lin Shu, Mai Kai, Hao Shumin, Yabuki Keiichi, Rennes, Reis, and Sato attended. Committee members Song Ziliang, Li Ming, Yoshida Seiji, and Lan Bo Malle were excused. In addition to passing the minutes of the previous meeting, the secretary reported that the committee had supervised and stamped 49 Class B (880 fineness) factory bars in November of the 25th year, and had supervised and sealed four types of subsidiary coins: 5.18 million 20-cent nickel coins, 3.56 million 10-cent nickel coins, 32.94 million 1-cent copper coins, and 2.4 million 1/2-cent copper coins. All were approved for release from the factory and reported in a list. The regular meeting approved all reports. The meeting adjourned at 5:00 PM.

Pudong Fellow Association Writes to Request Exemption of Housing Donation for Residents, Letter to Chuansha County 114

The Pudong Fellow Association sent a letter to the Chuansha County government to request exemption of housing donation for residents. The original letter is as follows:

According to letters from our members in Chuansha, Chen Caiqin, Wang Zhongming, Ding Zhengdong, etc., the Chuansha County government has recently sent personnel to collect housing donations from residents. The regulations and commencement dates were not announced in advance. When asked, the collectors stated that the funds were for expanding public security expenses, starting from July of this year, etc. Although public security expenses are important for maintaining local security, these expenses have traditionally been covered by surtaxes on land taxes, tea donations, and housing donations from shops. Chuansha is a small place with limited towns. Even if there is a need to expand public security facilities and increase the number of police officers, it can be covered by adjusting the existing donations and taxes. There is no need to add new taxes. Moreover, there was news of implementing housing donation in 1935, which was approved for postponement by various public organizations and fellow associations in the province. In April of this year, the Chuansha County government convened an administrative meeting, listing the collection of housing donation on the agenda, preparing to submit it for discussion. However, because of a deep understanding of the suffering of the people and the difficulty in bearing the burden, the county magistrate withdrew the proposal on the spot, indicating a postponement. Unexpectedly, only a few months later, personnel were dispatched to collect it, and it must be traced back to the beginning of July of this year, which is quite surprising. If it is done by the provincial government, then 61 counties of the province should be required to do it simultaneously. The investigation shows that the Shanghai and Nanhui counties adjacent to my Chuansha have not yet held it. Wujin then held it and then it was approved to be postponed, which is also seen in the newspapers. The areas of Shanghai, Nanhui, and Wujin are larger than Chuansha, and the security relationship is more important than that of Chuansha. How can Chuansha County alone open up the collection first, failing to enjoy its benefits? It is even more difficult to understand. As for the provisional measures for supervising local finance, provincial taxes should be planned by the provincial government, consulted by the Ministry of Finance for review and endorsement, and submitted to the Executive Yuan for review and transferred to the Legislative Yuan for resolution, and then submitted to the National Government for decree. County local taxes should be planned by the county government, convene local legal groups, open for discussion, submit to the Department of Finance for review and endorsement, and submit to the Provincial Government for resolution and decree, and consult with the Ministry of Finance for record. It is unknown to local Chuansha if the housing donation has gone through the procedures of the Legislative Yuan and the National Government. If it is a county local tax, then it has not gone through the procedures of convening local legal groups for public discussion, which is also not appropriate. Since the January 28th Incident, Chuansha has been affected by the general social depression. The countryside has collapsed and commerce has declined. Even those with some real estate have no income to look forward to. It is already difficult to maintain life, so how can they bear the burden of increased donations and taxes? This is the real situation that the members believe that housing donation cannot be collected.

All the people of Chuansha have the same opinion. In addition to submitting a separate letter to the Jiangsu Provincial Government, Department of Finance, and Chuansha County Government to revoke the original plan and stop the collection, we hereby request you to convey the public opinion of the Chuansha people and request that the housing donation be exempted. Regarding the provincial housing donation, our association telegraphed the provincial government on March 20 of last year to request exemption. The situation reported by our members Chen Caiqin, etc., in their letter this time, that Chuansha should not be collected is also true. We hereby write to your county and request that you comply with public opinion and exempt the collection.

Kong Xiangrong Mourns Mother's Death; Kong Resigns to Observe Mourning Period; Central Government Grants One Month Leave 115

The mother of Kong Xiangrong, Chairman of the Yellow River Conservancy Commission, passed away in Shanghai due to illness. Mr. Kong was deeply grieved by this sudden misfortune. Having arrived in Shanghai from Bianliang the day before yesterday, he immediately submitted his resignation to observe the mourning period. However, the Central Government, considering the Yellow River's winter flood prevention preparations and the importance of addressing the ice floe season, deemed it inappropriate for him to abruptly relinquish his responsibilities. He was granted a one-month leave to manage the funeral arrangements. Mr. Kong, along with his younger brothers, Xiangmian and Xiangxian, plans to escort his late mother's coffin back to their ancestral home in Qufu within a few days. A date will then be chosen for holding the memorial service and burial. In accordance with his late mother's will and the traditional rites of the Kong family, all funeral arrangements will be simplified as much as possible, given the current national crisis.

The late Madam Kong passed away at 12:00 noon on the 11th at her residence at 106 Avenue Grouchy in the French Concession, where the preliminary encoffining took place. The telegrams of condolence received that day from various parties included those from Han Fuju, Chairman of Shandong Province; Shen Honglie, Mayor of Qingdao; Zhang Shaotang, Secretary-General of the Shandong Provincial Government; Zhang Honglie, Director of the Department of Reconstruction; Hu Jiafeng, Secretary-General of the Qingdao Municipal Government; Chu Zhen, Director of the Department of Social Affairs; Zhou Jiacan, Counselor; Guo Binghe, Director of the Bureau of Finance; Xu Sen, Section Chief; Shen Baixian, Director of the Jiangsu Construction Department; Lu Peizhang, Secretary-General of the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing; Li Tang, Director of the National Treasury Department; Gao Bingfang, Director of the Tax Department; Tao Lujian, Vice Minister of the Interior; Qin Fen, Secretary-General of the National Economic Council; Zheng Zhaojing, Director of the Water Conservancy Department; Zhang Hanying, Deputy Director; Tang Kesan, Member of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission; Lin Jiqing, Member of the Shandong Provincial Government; Song Xishang of the Nanjing Public Works Bureau; He Bingru, Standing Committee Member of the Shandong Journalists Association; Ling Changyan, President of the Pingjin Telegraphic News Agency; Zhao Qi, former Director-General of the Jiaozhou Commercial Port; and Kong Decheng, Sacrificial Official to the Sage Confucius. In total, over a hundred telegrams arrived in Shanghai. The elegiac couplets and plaques received included those from Xiong Xiling, former Prime Minister; Kong Xiangxi, Vice President of the Executive Yuan and concurrently Minister of Finance; Zhu Ziqiao, Chairman of the Relief Work Committee; Wang Yiting, Chairman of the Central Disaster Relief Reserve Fund Management Committee; Fu Rulin, Central Committee Member and Chairman of the Yangtze River Conservancy Commission; Qu Yingguang, former Governor of Zhejiang Province; and Yu Hongqi, Member of the Control Yuan, among dozens of others. At noon on the 12th, the coffin was moved to the Chinese Funeral Home on Hart Road, and the major encoffining took place at 2:00 PM. Those from various circles who came to offer condolences included Xiong Xiling; Tan Zhonghui, representing Minister Kong; Tao Fuqing, representing Zhu Ziqiao; Guo Dehua, representing Qin Fen; as well as Qu Yingguang, Fu Rulin, Ye Zhuotang, Yang Jin, Zhang Du, Wang Lai, Li Wushen, Yin Tong, Zhao Lanping, Yang Zhixiong, Chen Jian'an, Chen Huahua, Chen Liting, Zheng Zhao, Hu Chunlin, Tang Zaijun, and Zhou Qibang, among over 500 people. Around 6:00 PM, Xiong Xiling, noting the late Madam's lifelong dedication to charitable causes and her role as one of the presidents of the World Red Swastika Society Women's Moral Society, led the presidents of the entire Shanghai branch of the World Red Swastika Society to the funeral home to pay their respects. It was said that the white carriages and horses on Hart Road displayed utmost solemnity.

Qin and Fu, Deputy Managers of the Currency Reserve Bank, Resign; Chen Lishan to Succeed on New Year's Day 116

Qin Jinqing, Manager of the Currency Joint Reserve Bank, after suffering from pleurisy and undergoing treatment by renowned physicians, is gradually recovering. However, the doctors advised him to rest due to overwork. Simultaneously, Fu Shenggui, Deputy Manager, was appointed as the Manager of Xinyu Money Exchange, making it impossible for him to concurrently hold both positions. Both submitted their resignations one after another. The Executive Committee of the Bank, noting that since its establishment on October 6, 1932, the currency reserves of the member exchanges had increased from three million yuan to over forty million yuan, establishing an exceptionally solid foundation and stabilizing the member exchanges, credited this achievement to Manager Qin. After repeated but unsuccessful attempts to retain him, his resignation was reluctantly approved. Chen Lishan was appointed to succeed him as Manager, scheduled to take office on New Year's Day. Mr. Chen was the former Manager of Baochang Money Exchange and a past Executive Committee member of the Guild. The position of Deputy Manager will be abolished, with Assistant Managers Qian Jingqiu and Yuan Wenyi continuing in their roles.

Shanghai West Silk Factory Workers Petitioned Party and Government Yesterday 118

Over five hundred workers from the Baohua, Yucun, and Yiyou silk weaving factories in Caojiadu, Yidingpan Road in this city, following the labor dispute that erupted on the evening of the 10th, remain in a stalemate due to the firm stances of both labor and management. Yesterday morning, six neighboring factories, including Yongfeng, briefly went on strike. The workers petitioned the Party and government authorities, as well as Du Yuesheng, Yu Qiaqing, and Wang Xiaolai for assistance. The Dagongshe reporter provides the following account of the situation:

Support from Various Factories

The Baohua, Yucun, and Yiyou silk weaving factories had previously dismissed workers without cause, leading to a dispute. Following an order from the Social Bureau, the dismissed workers were permitted to return to work. However, the factories refused to reinstate them, resulting in a strike. Yesterday marked the third day of the strike, which continues with relatively good order. Around 6:00 AM yesterday morning, over a thousand workers from six factories near the three factories, including Yongfeng, Tiancheng, Fuxing, and Jingcheng, went on strike in support. However, the labor union sent representatives to dissuade them, and they resumed work as usual. Nevertheless, the workers' emotions are tense, and if the issue is not resolved, the strike may spread.

Workers' Petition

Yesterday morning, the workers sent representatives, including Jin Xiuwen and twenty-three others, to petition the Municipal Party Headquarters, the Social Bureau, the General Labor Union, as well as Du Yuesheng, Wang Xiaolai, and Yu Qiaqing. Zhou Funong, Director of the People's Livelihood Section, received them at the Municipal Party Headquarters. Wang Xianqing of the Mediation Section received them at the Social Bureau. Zhou Xuexiang, a standing committee member, received them at the General Labor Union. Regarding the workers' requests, they promised to send representatives to mediate the matter immediately, urging the workers to await a resolution calmly and refrain from any excessive actions. Du, Wang, and Yu all comforted the workers, urging them to return to work and promising to persuade the factories to accept the government's orders. The workers expressed satisfaction and returned to the labor union to report around 12:00 noon.

Party Headquarters' Statement

A responsible member of the Labor Movement Committee at the Municipal Party Headquarters stated to the Dagongshe reporter yesterday that while the workers were acting on orders to return to work, only to be rejected by the factories, their hasty strike was inappropriate. As for the factories' attitude, if they remain stubborn and refuse to accept the decisions of the Party and government authorities, they should also bear corresponding responsibility. Currently, the only point of contention is the reinstatement of the dismissed workers. If both labor and management show some flexibility, the labor dispute can be easily resolved. The Municipal Party Headquarters will strive to mediate a solution to prevent its escalation.

Mediation Fails

The Dagongshe reporter learned that management had attempted to enlist a prominent figure to mediate yesterday. However, after detailed discussions, management still refused to accept the workers' minimum demands: (1) Reinstating all dismissed workers in accordance with the Social Bureau's instructions; (2) Providing dismissed workers with three months' severance pay, calculated at one yuan per month. As a result, no agreement was reached. It is now reported that the Party and government authorities have decided to conduct further mediation in the hope of achieving an early resolution.

Chief Prosecutor Sun Summoned Bail Bondsmen Again Yesterday; Shi Liang Sent Letter Requesting Extension; Letter from Guanqian Street, Suzhou; Appropriate to Surrender to Higher Court Nearby 119

Female lawyer Shi Liang, along with Shen Junru, Wang Zaoshi, Sha Qianli, Li Gongpu, Zhang Naiqi, Zou Taofen, and others, were arrested late at night on July 22. The following day, the Third Branch of the Higher Court ordered her release on bail, requiring her defense lawyers, Tang Hao and Zhang Zhirang, to act as guarantors. After being released on bail, Shi immediately left Shanghai and has not reported to the authorities. Subsequently, the Prosecutor's Office of the Third Branch of the Higher Court, citing Shi's escape while on bail, issued a warrant for her arrest. Considering the responsibility of lawyers Tang and Zhang, they were ordered to appear before the Prosecutor's Office of the Special No. 2 Court. Chief Prosecutor Sun Shaokang convened a hearing, ordering Tang and Zhang to each post a cash bond of 500 yuan, with a ten-day deadline to produce Shi Liang. Tang and Zhang, along with Shi's family, published notices in the newspapers urging Shi Liang to report to the authorities immediately, as previously reported in this newspaper. As the ten-day deadline for Tang and Zhang was approaching, the Prosecutor's Office of the Special No. 2 Court summoned Tang Hao and Zhang Zhirang again yesterday morning. Chief Prosecutor Sun Shaokang, accompanied by a clerk, questioned them in the Second Criminal Court, asking whether Shi Liang had reported to the authorities today. Lawyer Zhang Zhirang replied that he and Lawyer Tang had telegraphed Lawyer Dong asking if he knew Shi Liang's whereabouts. Dong replied that he did not know where Shi was. The day before yesterday (the 10th), he received a letter from Shi Liang from 80 Guanqian Street, Suzhou, in her own handwriting. He submitted the letter, stating that according to Shi's letter, she had returned to her hometown to visit her grandmother after being released on bail and had intended to report to the authorities on time. However, she unexpectedly suffered from hemoptysis and was unable to report. She requested an extension of one week, at which time she would be able to report and await questioning. Chief Prosecutor Sun then stated that, both legally and morally, Shi Liang should report to the authorities as soon as possible and that it would be appropriate for her to surrender to the Higher Court in Suzhou. If she surrendered to this court, she would not be made to feel uncomfortable. Lawyers Zhang and Tang then expressed their intention to publish another notice, urging Shi Liang to report to the authorities as soon as possible. Chief Prosecutor Sun then announced a postponement to the 19th, for further review. Shi Liang should report to await questioning by that time. If she is truly ill and unable to move, the court can conduct an on-site interrogation in accordance with the law to clarify the situation. After the statement, the court adjourned.

The Shanghai County Government, noting that the county's rice borer control efforts in 1935 were unsuccessful due to delayed preparations, has actively addressed the problem this year. Sudden Decrease in Copper Coin Exchange Rate 122

Since the Ministry of Finance implemented the legal tender system, the exchange rate in this city has been stable, with each legal tender coin exchanging for 312 copper coins. Double copper coins exchange for forty-five or forty-six coins, and double hao coins exchange for fifty copper coins. However, yesterday at noon, there was a significant shortage of copper coins in this city, causing small money exchanges and cigarette vendors to display exchange rates of only 280 or 289 copper coins per legal tender coin. The exchange rate for double copper coins remained unchanged. The discrepancy in the exchange rate for copper coins increased by as much as 134 coins within a few hours.

Shanghai Customs Issues Notice Restricting Explosive Materials 123

The Shanghai Customs Superintendent, Chang Nian, and the Commissioner of Customs, Baironson, have issued Joint Notice No. 1555, in accordance with orders to classify mono- and di-nitro organic compounds as explosive materials and restrict their transport. The notice states: "In accordance with the order of the Ministry of Finance, 'Mono- and di-nitro organic compounds' should be added to the list of prohibited articles and restricted or prohibited transport items under the 'Explosive Materials' category. This order must be strictly followed. All merchants are hereby notified accordingly. This notice is hereby issued."

Rong and Zhao, Facing Doors Opposite Each Other, Lawsuit Over Broken Chastity; Zhao Xing Sues Rong Erbao, Claiming She Was Violated and Happiness Sacrificed 124

Rong Erbao, also known as Er Yang, a Wuxi native residing at 35 Shenyu Lane, Tiantong Road, whose father is the founder of the Sanxin Shipping Company, and Rong Shaoqing, the cook he employed, are being sued by Zhao Xing, a Liyang woman residing at 18 Ruiqing Lane, Dongjiaxing Road, for offenses against public morals. The indictment states that Zhao Xing's daughter, Zhao Genhua, now twenty years old, was employed as a servant at the Rongchang household at 41 Shenyu Lane, Tiantong Road. Rong Erbao, who lived in the lane in a house facing theirs, seeing that Zhao Genhua was young and attractive and that she was naive and easily deceived, colluded with his cook on September 11 of this year to lure Zhao to his home on the upper floor, where he forcibly raped her. Because she was weak and unable to resist, she was violated. Afterward, Rong Erbao falsely claimed that his wife was often ill after childbirth and that if anything happened to her, he would take Zhao as his successor, or at least as a concubine, never going back on his words. Zhao, being young and inexperienced, was seduced, and her chastity was broken. Subsequently, on the 17th of the same month and on October 3, she was lured to his house and raped twice more. Zhao Xing believes that her daughter, who has not yet been betrothed, has been violated without cause, and her happiness for the rest of her life has been sacrificed. Rong Erbao, the first defendant, committed the egregious acts of luring and raping Zhao Genhua, violating Articles 229 and 241 of the Criminal Code. Rong Shaoqing, the second defendant, is guilty of violating Article 240, Section 2 of the same code. Therefore, the plaintiff brings this suit, requesting punishment. Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, Judge Xiao Xie-Fen presided over the Second Criminal Court and summoned the two defendants, who were not present. Lawyer Mao Fengwu appeared in court as their representative. Judge Xiao, after briefly questioning the plaintiff, Zhao Xing, and Zhao Genhua, adjourned the case for further hearing on the afternoon of the 22nd.

Ye Fu-kang Embezzlement Case; Judge Cross-Examines Witnesses; Hu Jin-kun Details Events; Ye Fu-kang Denies Reconciliation 125

Ye Fu-kang, a lawyer who formerly served as a judge in the Shanghai District Court and now runs a hat shop selling "Little Luzon" hats, was accused by Wang Hanqing, a Henan native who formerly worked as a detective in Hankou, of embezzling his vast fortune under the guise of defending him in a theft case in 1931. The Ministry of Justice ordered the District Court to investigate. Prosecutor Tang Ru-xiu released Ye Fu-kang on a cash bail of 20,000 yuan and indicted him for embezzlement. Yesterday morning, Judge Lu Hong-shi presided over a continued hearing in the Fourth Criminal Court. Ye Fu-kang was defended by lawyer Yu Chengxiu. The judge questioned witness Hu Jin-kun, 39 years old, a Hubei native who formerly lived in the Nanshan pier in Pudong and now resides at 23 Yongxing Lane, Tangshan Road, Xiahaimiao. He stated that he did not know Ye Fu-kang, but Wang Hanqing was his friend. Wang was arrested for theft in March 1931 and initially hired lawyer Fan Gang, who was recommended by Li Zhanyuan, for a fee of 3,000 yuan. Wang Hanqing's wife, Wang Zhangshi, and his brother Wang Fuyou's wife, Wang Yangshi, went to the police station to visit him but were also detained, and two banknotes worth 2,000 and 5,000 yuan, as well as sixteen gold ornaments, were confiscated. He did not know who hired Ye Fu-kang. Wang Hanqing was released in April. After Wang's release, he did not meet with him. The two women were released first. They had a total of 10,000 yuan deposited in Juxingcheng Bank. He withdrew 4,000 yuan, gave 200 yuan to Wang Yangshi, and deposited the remaining 3,800 yuan in Zhejiang Xingye Bank, including a 3,000 yuan fixed deposit and an 800 yuan current account. He gave the 800 yuan in the current account to Wang Yangshi. The banknotes were given to Li Zhanyuan. He was not present when they were given to Ye Fu-kang by Wang Yangshi and Wang Zhangshi. Questioned about Ye Fu-kang's claim that the banknotes were in his possession and that he refused to hand them over, resulting in the publishing of a notice declaring them invalid, he replied that this was not true. He did not know how much was paid to Fan Gang. When asked if Wang Hanqing had gone to Shanghai in 1933 to ask Ye for money, he replied yes, he returned 5,000, but he did not know who handled the process. In 1935, he received 500 yuan at lawyer Gu Ao's office. When asked about Gu Ao's saying 1300 yuan, he stated, "I do not know how much they secretly transferred." Wang came again this year. Because Wang Zhangshi had died and his daughter, Cui Bao, was getting married, he was going back. When asked whether there had been a reconciliation, he replied that Ye Fu-kang had taken a 20,000 yuan bail receipt and asked lawyer Gu Ao to tell Wang to settle the matter for 10,000 yuan. Wang said that the money was not in his hand and that he wanted to vent his anger in court. He and Wang had stayed at 11 Central Apartments, Pushi Road, for one night, and Gu Ao had also come to discuss reconciliation. Furthermore, Cao San-ye called Gu Ji-rong's law office on October 23 to discuss reconciliation, but it was unsuccessful. The document submitted by Wang Hanqing was not a withdrawal of the charges but a statement that the money had been taken by a woman. Gu Ji-rong drafted the document, and Gu said that it did not matter and that the lawsuit could still be pursued. Gu Ji-rong was recommended by Li Song-tang. Asked why, if there was no reconciliation and he did not receive any money, he would admit wrongdoing, he replied that he did not know the inside story. Asked whether Wang Hanqing had seen the document, he replied that Wang Hanqing was illiterate and that Gu Ji-rong read it to him. The judge then stated that if Ye Fu-kang was innocent, then Wang Hanqing had made several inconsistent statements and should be charged with false accusation. Furthermore, his previous statements were inconsistent. If he wanted to make a statement, why didn't he do so in court, instead of making a statement admitting false accusations? This was very strange. Do you know his place of origin? He replied that it was Laiyang County, Henan, but he did not know the detailed address. The judge ordered an investigation to locate him and bring him to court. Hu Jin-kun repeatedly agreed. The judge then questioned witness Li Song-tang, 44 years old, a Shaoxing native who works as a ticket inspector for the Shanghai Tram Company and resides at 327 Huishan Road. He stated that he did not know Wang Hanqing, but was introduced to him by a friend, Li Yingxiang, who lived at his place. Li has now returned home due to unemployment and is not in Shanghai. He has forgotten whether Wang Hanqing hired Gu Ji-rong to draft the document on October 8 or 9. Because Wang Hanqing was anxious to go home, he wanted to draft a document. There was no fee, only a document fee of 2.4 yuan. Gu Ji-rong wrote the draft in pencil. He did not understand what they were talking about or what they were writing. Two or three days after the document was submitted, Wang Hanqing left without saying goodbye and never returned. At this point, the judge summoned Ye Fu-kang to court and questioned him about the witnesses' testimonies, asking if there had been any reconciliation. Ye replied that there had been none at all. The judge then stated that he would adjourn the case to investigate further and summon Wang Hanqing for further questioning.

Wu A-kang, Waterborne Gambler of the Dongyang Company, Apprehended; Water Police Speedboat Pursued and Arrested; Most Gamblers Escaped 127

Gambling on the Huangpu River in Hongkou has long been rampant, with three gambling dens operating on Changjiang passenger ships docked at the wharves of the Dongyang Company, Ewo Company, and Taikoo Company. The Dongyang Company wharf is the original den, while Ewo and Taikoo are newer. (Recently, due to strict police raids and shallow waters on the Yangtze River, few ships are available, so only the Dongyang Company operates, hiring barges or dockside vessels and mooring them in the middle of the Huangpu River to gather people for gambling. The games offered include Tongbao, Yaotun, and Twenty-One Points, and they employ numerous accomplices to serve as lookouts at key locations on land and water. If they spot police boats approaching, they signal, and the gamblers quickly row the boat to the wharf and scatter to escape, making arrests difficult.) Around 5:00 PM the day before yesterday, the gamblers hired a boat and moored in the middle of the Huangpu River in Hongkou for gambling. Detectives from the Water Police Station discovered this and immediately led officers on a patrol boat at full speed to make arrests. The gamblers spotted them and immediately rowed the barge close to the Dongyang Company wharf to disembark and escape, but the detectives had already surrounded them from behind. The operator, Wu A-kang (a Ningbo native), was arrested, but the others escaped. Wu and the gambling equipment were taken to the Water Police Station. After questioning by the station chief, Wu A-kang and the gambling equipment were transferred to the District Court yesterday. After a brief interrogation by the prosecutor, he was ordered to be detained pending prosecution.

Spring Plowing Concerns: Cattle Plague Discovered in the Suburbs; Animal Disease Prevention Institute Dispatches Doctors for Examination; Public Notice Sets Deadline to Visit the Institute for Injections 130

Recently, cattle plague has been discovered in this city, especially among the draft cattle in the suburbs. Therefore, the Jiangwan Animal Disease Prevention Institute of this city has repeatedly dispatched veterinarians to the countryside for examination. The results show that the diseases suffered, in addition to arthritis, also include foot-and-mouth disease. The institute believes that if prevention and treatment are not carried out quickly, it will be enough to affect farming. Therefore, a public notice is issued stating: Recent outbreaks of cattle plague have occurred in Shanghai. In order to curb the spread of the disease and eradicate it as soon as possible, all dairy farms and farmers in this city who need injections of anti-cattle plague serum for the purpose of preventing cattle plague should have the cattle owners or representatives come to the institute to register the number of cattle to be injected within three days, namely the 14th, 15th, and 16th of this month. The institute will immediately dispatch veterinarians to administer the serum injections in order of registration. All expenses will be waived. It is hoped that everyone will register as soon as possible and not delay themselves. Animal Disease Prevention Institute. (Office hours) 8:00 AM to 12:00 PM, 1:30 PM to 5:00 PM. (Address) 400 Xianggu Road, Shanghai.

Fire Insurance Claim Reward Payments Are Being Processed for Completion 134

After the January 28th Incident, the residents of Zhabei suffered a great disaster. Some of those who had fire insurance were promoted by Yu Qiaqing, Fang Jiaobo, Wang Binyan, Tang Youwei, Ye Jiaxing, and others to organize the Disaster Area Fire Insurance Claim Association to negotiate with various insurance companies based on reason. However, because it involved war, the insurance companies were unable to bear the responsibility for compensation. After several months of effort, little progress was made. Therefore, the policyholder meeting publicly elected Hu Yibo, Xu Zaikang, Wang Zhixiang, Mu Yueqiu, Ma Rugen, and others to form a claims committee to intensify the claims work. Soon, due to financial exhaustion, it was suspended halfway for almost half a year. The committee members Wang Zhixiang, Xu Zaikang, Mu Yueqiu, Ma Rugen, Liang Baolin, and others, deeply concerned about the interruption of the association's work and the unfinished mission, re-invited enthusiastic committee members to continue planning and received financial support from the sponsors of the association, Fang Jiaobo, Chen Songyuan, Ye Jiaxing, Mo Meiqing and other committee members, thus enabling the re-energized claims work from Jiaotong Road in Zhabei to take off. At that time, society sympathized, public opinion supported, and the municipal government and the Social Affairs Bureau mediated. Yu Juntianbi was especially diligent in his efforts. Therefore, in less than a month, 19 Hua Shang Insurance companies jointly provided 10,000 yuan as an initiative for relief. More than 150 foreign insurance companies were mediated by Ye Weiyi of the Social Affairs Bureau. After years of effort, they received a similar 20,000 yuan for relief. The funds were held in trust by the Social Affairs Bureau. After two policyholders' meetings in January of the Republic of China year 24, they resolved the distribution method. The re-elected claims committee members and policyholders who participated in the claims were entitled to rewards and bonuses. It was approved by the Social Affairs Bureau, and payments were made in batches as recorded. Now it is heard that the rewards for the claims committee members have been largely completed, but the bonuses for the policyholders have been outstanding for three years due to numerous relocations. The person in charge of distributing the funds, in order to expedite the completion, has published notices in Shen Bao and Xin Bao newspapers on the 4th, 5th, and 6th of this month to register and urge collection. For the registration procedure, one only needs to state the name, address, and the number of times they participated in the claims at Jiaotong Road and mail it to Shen Bao mailbox number 391 before the 15th of this month.

Fire at Qin Feng Factory on Saposai Road; Spreads to Jiu Yi Hosiery Factory 135

The Qin Feng Cotton Weaving Factory at 450 Saposai Road in the French Concession was opened by Gu Yiqin from Wuxi for many years with a capital of hundreds of thousands of gold. Previously, it was engaged in weaving silk products. Recently, due to the sluggish market, it switched to operating cotton textiles. In April of this year, after moving to a new location at 162 Rue du Pere Froc, the old site was converted into a warehouse to store raw materials such as cotton. More than a dozen flower-picking female workers worked there every day. At 10 AM yesterday, a fire suddenly broke out in the factory's warehouse. The female workers noticed it and rushed out to inform the accounting room to report to the fire brigade. The fire engine immediately rushed to the scene to put out the fire. It had already spread to the neighboring Jiu Yi Hosiery Factory. After an hour of firefighting, the fire was extinguished. At that time, the French police station heard the alarm and immediately dispatched a large number of detectives to rush to the scene to suppress the situation. Afterwards, the police station learned that the Qin Feng Factory warehouse had several thousand gold in fire insurance, while the Jiu Yi Hosiery Factory had moved its machinery and materials to the new factory on Yuezhou Road and Feihong Road in Hongkou three or four days ago. Therefore, the loss of the old factory yesterday was only several thousand gold. The police station is currently investigating the cause of the fire to determine the appropriate action.

Xiang Qizhang from Anhui recently set up a private opium den at 61 Pu'ai Fang, Zhoujiapai Road, for people to smoke opium for profit. Lawsuit Involving Mother, Son, and Wife 137

Xie Juxiu, 32 years old from Tongzhou, is currently a rickshaw puller. He currently lives at 2 Qingyun Li, Baoxing Road, Zhabei. His elderly mother, Xie Chen, 60 years old, and wife, Xie Lanying, 31 years old, live at 194 Chenjiabo, Caojiadu, West Shanghai. Unexpectedly, Xie, although a rickshaw puller, also learned the habits of urban youth, squandering and neglecting the lives of his mother and wife, and never returning home for four years. Although Xie Lanying had little schooling, a poor woman without education, she was quite virtuous. She worked in a factory every day, earning her hard-earned money to support her mother-in-law. Therefore, the mother-in-law and daughter-in-law did not feel cold and hungry because of the bad son's absence. But heaven did not bless them. Recently, Xie Lanying overworked herself and became ill, causing the mother-in-law and daughter-in-law to have no food to cook. She had no choice but to discuss life with her son, but was met with violence. Therefore, the mother-in-law and daughter-in-law were heartbroken and filed a complaint with the district court. Yesterday, Judge Xie held a hearing. The defendant did not appear. The old woman recounted the experience and said that when the son was eight years old, his father died. She endured hardship to raise him and arranged for Lanying to be a child bride. When he was 20 years old, she arranged for them to marry. Now he has abandoned his mother and wife for four years because my daughter-in-law is sick and cannot work. When I advised him, he became violent. Xie Lanying testified that she usually made 70 to 80 cents a day, which was enough to support herself, but now she is really sick and her husband is ungrateful and beats her. The official said, "Your mother, son, and wife cannot resolve the lawsuit. You are loving and helpful, which is very good, and your son's work and husband are also pitiful. You should go back and reconcile properly. The defendant will be summoned next time to resolve the matter." Then he adjourned the court.

A Large Number of Gamblers Punished for Having Many Hideouts; 29 Gamblers Arrested; Sentenced to Imprisonment and Fines 138

Chinese and Western detectives from the Laozha police station learned that Shen Jinbao, nicknamed "Qiao Pigu Jinbao" (翹屁股金寶, "翘屁股" literally means "翹 butt", a common local nickname), and others specialized in opening rooms in major hotels within their jurisdiction to gather people for gambling and skim profits. Therefore, they intensified their investigation. However, the places where Shen and others gambled were like rabbits with many hideouts, and they frequently changed their location, making it difficult to arrest them. The day before yesterday, they learned that they were in room 503 of the Xinxin Hotel and were about to go to arrest them, but Shen and others moved to room 240 of the Dadong Hotel on Nanjing Road and continued to gamble. Yun A'gen, the Chinese Chief Detective of the police station, ordered detectives at 11 PM the day before yesterday to rush to arrest them without making a sound. At that time, the gambling was in full swing. The detectives rushed in and arrested the bosses Shen Jinbao, Li Jinbao, Chen Zhulin, and gamblers Shen Xiaobao, Zhou Heqin, Wu Hangye, Li A'gou, Lin Zirong, Chen Jiuxia, Gu A'you, Zhang Heshang, and others, a total of 29 people. They confiscated gambling paraphernalia such as pai gow and mahjong tiles, and more than one hundred dollars in gambling money, and took them all to the police station. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the First Special District Court. Judge Ye Shengchao interrogated them. Qian Jiujiu, the police station's lawyer, prosecuted them for gathering to gamble and gambling and requested severe punishment. After questioning by Judge Ye, Li Jinbao was sentenced to two months in prison, Shen Jinbao and Chen Zhulin each to one month in prison, and the rest were each fined ten yuan as a warning. The gambling paraphernalia and gambling money were confiscated.

Ma Mingxia Dies from a Fall 141

Ma Fushan, 58 years old from Anhui, works as a relief worker at the Xinwei Relief Association attached to Renji Hall. He is currently in Xikang for relief work. His family resides at 25 Ningkang Li, Route Ghisi, French Concession. Ma's third son, Ma Mingxia, 28 years old, also works at the Xinwei Relief Association. On the night of the 11th at 11:30 PM, Mingxia was at home, climbing from the ground floor window to the table, intending to lower the window curtain. He lost control for a moment and fell from a height into the patio, causing head injuries and bleeding from the ears. His family immediately took him to Guangci Hospital. Due to the severity of his injuries, he died within half an hour of admission. The hospital reported to the French police station, who sent the body to the autopsy room of Tongren Fuyuan Branch Hall. Yesterday, they reported to the Chief Prosecutor of the Second Special Court, who confirmed that the deceased Ma Mingxia had died from a fall. The body was released to his mother, Ma Wang, for burial.

Bandit Zhu Sanmao Sentenced to Three Years and Six Months 142

Zhu Sanmao from Ningbo, at 8:30 PM on May 28th of this year, colluded with accomplices to rob Madame Rong Chen with weapons on Yuezhou Road, stealing gold jewelry worth 60 dollars and fleeing in different directions. The police station was notified and captured him. Recently, Liu Zhaonian, a Chinese detective from the Hongkou police station, and detectives Chen Baozhong and Wang Chonghao investigated and captured Zhu Sanmao, a bandit in this case. He confessed that his accomplice was named Xiao Liansheng, and Ni was his laotouzi (老師頭子, meaning "teacher," referring to his leader). The detectives then went to arrest Ni Yucai and took him to the First Special District Court. Zhu Sanmao's confession was the same as before, stating that Ni provided the gun, but Ni Yucai denied it. He was remanded and the investigation was postponed. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhong Qing presided over the continued hearing. Zhu Sanmao suddenly changed his testimony, saying that he had falsely accused Ni because he had failed to borrow money from Ni. He asked for leniency. Judge Zhong sentenced Zhu Sanmao to three years and eight months in prison and released Ni Yucai. The case was closed and the remaining ten dollars were taken away by Xiao Liansheng.

At 6 AM on the 12th, six plainclothes detectives, along with the police chief and police officers from the Cao Hang Town Public Security Substation, suddenly arrived at the home of Ding Boqi in Cao Hang Town, a county-administered town. Deposit Dispute at Dong Xin Hotel; Ren A'gen Dies by Suicide as a Result 144

The Dong Xin Hotel in Baoyu Li, Dongxinqiao Street, French Concession, was originally opened by Wang Derong. In May of this year, Wang Qingchu and Bian Jing'an jointly leased it for business. It was still operated under the original brand name with the addition of a "Yuji" (裕記) character. It was transferred and sublet to Xu Yusheng before its term was up. It received a security deposit of more than 2,800 yuan. The more than 1,400 yuan deposit paid by the waiters, Chen Dachang, Zuo Liyan, and others, was completely ignored. They could not get it back from those who owed it. Later, lawyer Gu Kenfu mediated and Wang Qingchu wrote a receipt promising to return the deposit to the waiters. When the deadline arrived, the waiters asked Gu for the money, but he was unable to pay. The waiters negotiated with Gu, and it even escalated into violence, but the money was still not received. Now, the waiters Chen Dachang and Zuo Liyan and ten others have hired a lawyer to file a fraud and injury case against Wang Qingchu and Gu Kenfu with the Criminal Court of the Second Special District Court. After one hearing, the case was rescheduled because the defendant did not appear. However, one of the waiters, Ren A'gen from Ningbo, committed suicide by taking poison because he could not recover his deposit. After it was discovered, he was sent to the hospital for treatment and recovered, but he still died due to the remaining poison. Yesterday, Judge Sun Penghai interrogated the case. The plaintiffs and their lawyers appeared in court and testified that the deposit was paid in front of Gu Kenfu and collected by Wang Qingchu, who issued a receipt. The receipt was presented as evidence. Only Gu Kenfu appeared as a defendant. Wang Qingchu sent a lawyer to appear on his behalf. According to Gu, when they paid the deposit, I and Wang Qingchu had not yet met. Three or four days after I met Tu Qingchu, the plaintiffs surrounded Wang Qingchu and demanded money at the Qinghe Hotel. Wang asked me to mediate. I wrote a receipt with a scheduled date. When the date arrived, Wang had no money to give me, so I had no money to pay the plaintiffs. The plaintiffs then went to my house and argued all night. After reporting to the police station, they dispersed. Later, Wang Qingchu gave me a check for 130 yuan and 60 to 70 yuan in cash, totaling 200 yuan, and asked me to go to the Dafang Hotel to reconcile with the plaintiffs. Because the plaintiffs did not want the check and needed cash, the reconciliation failed. He denied any joint fraud or injury. Wang Qingchu's defense lawyer stated that Wang could not appear in court due to illness and presented an account book to prove that he had paid the plaintiffs some money and wages and there was no fraud. The court examined the situation and, due to the lack of witnesses, ordered a rescheduling for the 19th for further interrogation.

Seeking Electrical Engineering Talents, Paid Internship in German Factory, Monthly Salary During Internship is One Hundred Yuan 151

The Shanghai Deutsch-Österreichische Vereinigung (German-Austrian Association) and alumni of Tongji University recently received a letter from the International Business Machines Corporation (IBM), entrusting them to seek a talented individual who is proficient in both English and German languages and a graduate of either the Department of Electrical Engineering or the Department of Mechanical Engineering. First University League Football Tournament Jinan Wins the Crusader Cup Yesterday's Final Six to Two Defeats Fudan Inheriting the Greatness of the Jiangda Era 161

The first University League Football Championship, which began last week, saw Jinan taking the lead with two wins in two games. Fudan had also defeated Guanghua. Although there was still one game against Tongji, the odds of winning were stable. Therefore, the Fudan and Jinan teams have become evenly matched in the competition. The two teams met in Zhenru yesterday, and the key to success or failure was highly contested. The battle was tense and fierce throughout. However, Fudan lacked footwork, so it was overwhelmed by Jinan with a score of six to two.

After the exchange, Jinan attacked first. After about fifteen minutes of stalemate, Fudan's left forward, Fang Baoling, received support from the left and registered the first goal. However, one minute later, Jinan launched a fierce attack again. Right forward Liang Yaohua broke out of the crowd and shot low, hitting the target. The score was tied at one to one. Ten minutes later, Jinan's center forward, Wu Shufang, scored another goal, exceeding the score to two to one. The first half ended with this score. After Jinan took the lead, Jinan became more and more courageous and the offensive became more intense. Fudan had been too defensive in the first half, leading to the backwardness, so it changed to an offensive strategy. Unexpectedly, the defense was slightly relaxed, so Jinan took advantage of the opportunity to enter. Jie Yaohua scored first in five minutes, increasing the score to three to one. Soon Xue Yongyuan also shot in the free throw line, and the situation was even more superior with four to one. Then Cai Jincai got the ball from the left wing and touched it into the net, making it five to one. Fudan also counterattacked fiercely at this time. Fang Baoling and Liu Zuxiu were the most active, but they failed to get the desired result due to lack of response. Before long, Fudan's hinterland was once again trapped by Jinan. Wu Shufen passed in from the sideline, and the landing point was excellent. Cai Jincai touched the ground and hit the crossbar again, and the posture was wonderful, which was rare. Jinan led with six to one, and the championship was stable. Liang Yaohua also withdrew due to injury, and Zhang Minzhi replaced him. Fudan's forwards did not give up despite the fact that hope was gone, and still fought back hard. Ten minutes from the end of the game, Li Changchi passed in from the sideline, passing over the goal. Liu Zuxiu caught up and picked it up, bouncing from the top of the crossbar. The battle ended with a score of six to two. Jinan won the first University League Championship with three wins in three games, inheriting the greatness of the Jiangda era. Referee Chen Jixiang.

Major Changes to the 1936-37 Basketball Rules: Notice to Members from the Shanghai Basketball Association 167

The Secretariat of the Shanghai Basketball Association announces that this year's games will be conducted according to the new 1936-37 rules. Currently, the official rulebooks have not yet arrived in Shanghai. We have only received a notice from the American Referees Association outlining the major changes. This notice has been translated and published for the benefit of members. Fortunately, the changes are simple and easy to remember.

(1) A large circle with a radius of six and a half feet is added outside the center circle of the court. During the jump ball, other players may not enter the circle before the jumper touches the ball.

(2) Each team is allowed to call four "time-outs" during each game (previously three under the old rules).

(3) The restriction on offensive players in the free-throw area within the semicircle farthest from their own basket for three seconds is removed. That is, the effective area of the 3-second rule is reduced.

(4) The rule that "substitute players may not speak with players on the court before the start of the game" is removed.

(5) If a defender touches the hand of a player holding the ball with one or both hands, it will not be considered a "hitting" personal foul.

All new and old members should promptly complete the membership and registration procedures at this office. (Old members should pay a registration fee and security deposit of 5 national currency units each and obtain a registration form from this office. B-group teams should also submit a photo of each player.) New members must pay a membership fee of 10 national currency units in addition to the above procedures. Those who have not completed the procedures clearly will not be allowed to participate in the games. Please pay attention to this.

Yesterday's Western Union First Division Football Match: Donghua Again Defeats St. Francis 3-1, Leading Only 1-0 in the First Half 172

Donghua and St. Francis met again yesterday at Yi Garden in the Western Union First Division football match. As a result, Donghua won 4-1. Donghua's lineup was depleted, with half of the players from the B team. They missed two penalty kicks in yesterday's match. Here is a brief account of yesterday's battle:

First Half

St. Francis attacked first. After 8 minutes of stalemate, Donghua got a penalty opportunity. Sun Jinshun scored the penalty, opening the scoring. After that, although Donghua's attack was strong, they were unlucky and missed several chances. Soon after, St. Francis's right-back, Shi Dengge, committed a foul, and another penalty was awarded. Luo Haiguang took the kick but missed. Because Su Shi moved on his own when Luo raised his foot, a retake was awarded. Luo Haiguang took the second kick, but it was still blocked by Su Shi. Soon after, Luo shot from the 15-yard mark, but the shot was weak and was caught. The first half ended with Donghua leading 1-0.

Second Half

After lemonade, St. Francis gradually became active. After 15 minutes, Joni Ho shot from the sideline, Zhang Rongcai caught it but then lost it, Huilai rushed up and kicked it into the net, making it equal. The morale was boosted. Zhang Rongcai, with both hands and feet, saved two critical shots. After 20 minutes, Jia Youliang dribbled forward and passed to Wu Naho on the left baseline, who shot forcefully into the goal, putting Donghua ahead 2-1. Three minutes later, Jia Youliang and Wu Naho established contact, with the left and right wings assisting forward, rushing to the end. Both Jia and Wu were knocked to the ground. The ball bounced off Jia's leg and into the net, making it 3-1, securing Donghua's victory. Donghua won the game with a final score of 3-1. Yesterday's lineup was as follows:

Educational News

Guangdong's Measures for Students Studying Abroad: Twelve Students Selected to Study in Europe and America This Year 174

Guangdong Province held the third selection examination for publicly funded students to study abroad in June of this year, selecting twelve students to study in Europe and the United States, majoring in hydraulic engineering, hydroelectric engineering, mechanical engineering, military chemistry, ordnance manufacturing, shipbuilding, metallurgy, rayon, woolen agriculture, and education. The province provides the following benefits for students studying abroad: for those studying in Europe, 1,000 yuan for overseas travel and outfitting expenses, and the school fees will be paid in full. Each student will receive a monthly living allowance of 14 British pounds and 40 British pounds for return travel expenses. For those studying in the United States, 1,000 yuan for overseas travel and outfitting expenses will be given, and the school fees will be paid in full. Each student will receive a monthly living allowance of 75 US dollars and 300 US dollars for return travel expenses. This is the current situation for those studying abroad. Upon completion of their studies and return to the country, the provincial government will assign them to work in government agencies or factories. If publicly funded students engage in non-assigned jobs without government permission after graduation, they will be required to repay part or all of the public funds they received. Their salaries during their service period will be limited to 100 to 1000 yuan. Those who have served in government agencies, schools, or factories will be able to advance in their original salary scale when they return to serve, and the length of service will be the same as the length of the public funding. As for the measures for counties and cities to subsidize students studying abroad, each county and city must meet three conditions: (1) The county or city's approved education funds are not in arrears; (2) The county or city's compulsory education funds have been fully allocated in accordance with the province's interim measures for the implementation of compulsory education, with no delays; (3) The field of study of the students subsidized by the county or city is indeed particularly needed by the local county or city. The application must be submitted to the Department of Education for approval before subsidies can be granted. The fields of study subsidized for students should be limited to science, engineering, agriculture, medicine, and education. The students subsidized by each county and city should be recommended by the county to participate in the Department of Education's selection examination for publicly funded students studying abroad. After passing the examination and being approved by the Department, the county may issue subsidies. However, if the country and subject applied for are suitable for the provincial quota and public funding is provided by the province, the county subsidy will no longer be received. The subsidies allocated by each county and city to students studying abroad should not exceed 10% of the total county's educational funds.

Ministry of Education Orders All Middle Schools to Follow Teaching Hours 175

The Ministry of Education issued a circular to the education departments of all provinces and cities on the 11th, stating: "The table of teaching subjects and weekly teaching hours for each subject in junior and senior middle schools has been revised and promulgated by the Ministry in February of this year, and a circular has been issued stating that it will be implemented from the 25th academic year. Subsequently, the curriculum standards for each subject in junior and senior middle schools were revised and fully promulgated before June and a circular was issued ordering their implementation. In this academic year, all first and second grade students in junior and senior middle schools in all regions should follow the revised curriculum standards, and third grade students should follow the previously promulgated curriculum standards for teaching separately. There should be no changes or additions to the teaching subjects and hours. However, it has been found that many middle schools in various regions have not been able to strictly comply, and some have arbitrarily increased subjects and hours in preparation for the joint entrance examination and higher education, with the daily increase in hours exceeding the regulations by one or two hours. This will leave students with no free time to participate in extracurricular activities to improve their physical fitness, and no adequate rest time to recover from their fatigue, which will have a significant impact on the development of young people's physical and mental well-being. We hereby issue a circular to all departments, instructing all middle schools under their jurisdiction to pay close attention to rectification. Provincial supervisors should pay special attention to this during inspections, and severely correct any violations in order to comply with the law and emphasize efficiency. It is also hoped that all middle schools under their jurisdiction will be instructed to strictly comply. This is of utmost importance." In addition to separate orders, this order is issued for compliance.

Shen Bao Children's Special Issue

Little Friends, Let's Promote the "One Cent Movement" 186

— Xiao Bai

Thanks to the bravery of our front-line soldiers and the enthusiastic support of people across the country, the war in Suiyuan has achieved great victories. The recapture of Bailingmiao last week was the most glorious event of defeating the bandits and recovering lost territory.

Little friends! Aren't you happy and excited to hear this news of victory? However, at this moment, while we celebrate our victory, we must not forget our responsibility to love our country. We must know that this invasion of Suiyuan by the puppet bandits will not end completely with one defeat. They are preparing for a second and third large-scale invasion! Therefore, our support work in the rear should be redoubled and we should do our best!

Now people across the country have enthusiastically risen to engage in various support activities for Suiyuan, such as the "One-Day Movement," "One-Dollar Movement," "Reducing Food," and "Stopping Coal" heroic movements. But here, I want to propose a "One-Cent Movement" to children across the country. I hope that each of us children will donate one cent to contribute to the country, support Suiyuan, and fulfill our smallest responsibility to save the country!

I think this suggestion will definitely be echoed by children across the country, because although we are all young children and our power to save the country is the smallest, we all have a patriotic heart that everyone should have. Children with money can save a cent from candy and toys, and poor children can also save a cent from clothes and food. Send this money to the newspaper office or bank, etc., and remit it to the soldiers who are fighting hard on the front line. This is an easy task, but if tens of millions of children across the country can do it, then there will immediately be several million dollars to contribute to the warriors who are fighting bandits and killing thieves.

Little friends across the country! I hope you all discuss and work hard to promote this "One-Cent Movement"!

Idle Talk about Suiyuan 187

— Ying Dai

This invasion of Suiyuan by bandits has made the people of the country immediately pay attention to Suiyuan, and the support movement for Suiyuan is expanding daily. However, we believe that many people still do not clearly understand everything about Suiyuan. Therefore, I want to briefly introduce the evolution, transportation, products, and customs of Suiyuan here, so that children can also leave a deep impression in their minds.

Evolution: Suiyuan was designated as a special region in the third year of the Republic of China (1914), and it was not until the seventeenth year of the Republic of China (1928) that the special region was changed to a province, with Gui Sui as the provincial capital. Currently, it has four first-class counties: Gui Sui, Salachi, Baotou, and Fengzhen; four second-class counties: Wuchuan, Xinghe, Wuyuan, and Jining; and eight third-class counties: Tokto, Dongsheng, Liangcheng, Qingshuihe, Helin'er, Taolin, Guyang, and Linhe.

Transportation: Suiyuan's land transportation includes the Ping Sui Railway, which starts from Beiping, passes through Chahar and Shanxi, and ends at Baotou County in Suiyuan, with a length of about 750 kilometers, also known as the Ping Bao Railway. The future plan for this railway is to connect to the Long Hai Railway to the south and the Ping Han Railway and Jin Pei Railway to the southeast, forming a large circle. As for its functions, it is very convenient for national defense and has the hope of development in culture and commerce. As for highways, there are the Sui Zhang Road, Sui Meng Road, Xi Sui Road, Ning Bao Road, and Bao Dong Road, which are five major trunk lines with a total length of 1,400 kilometers, all of which are now open to traffic. In addition, there are 40 branch lines, with a length of 3,800 kilometers, of which one-third have not yet been built.

Agricultural Products: Suiyuan has fertile land and abundant agricultural products. Except for rice, which is not produced, wheat, barley, corn, sorghum, millet, glutinous millet, oats, buckwheat, soybeans, green beans, peas, mung beans, and soybeans are all produced, and the quantity is also considerable. In addition, the area already planted or not yet planted but suitable for forests is more than 100 million mu.

Animal Husbandry: According to the estimates of the Central Agricultural and Industrial Institute in the twenty-second year of the Republic of China (1933), Suiyuan Province mainly has 275,000 head of cattle, 93,000 horses, 37,000 mules, 61,000 donkeys, 3,297,000 sheep, with an average of more than 15 head per household, 1,704,000 pigs, with an average of 9 head per household, 2,181,000 chickens, with an average of more than 12 head per household, and 80,000 ducks, with an average of 0.2 head per household.

Customs: Although there are still many Mongol residents in Suiyuan, there are also many Han people who have migrated from Shanxi, Hebei, Shandong, Henan, and other places, especially Shanxi people. There have been immigrants from Shanxi in Suiyuan for one or two hundred years, and the number of people is large, so the customs and human feelings are not very different from Shanxi. Marriages between men and women are still based on the orders of parents and the words of matchmakers, with very little autonomy. When people die, the rich use extremely luxurious clothes, coffins, and burn ghost money, and chanting sutras by monks is also unavoidable. Wealthy families are very lively when they raise sons, celebrate the full moon, and celebrate the hundredth day.

Parasitism 188

— Zhen

One Sunday morning, not long after Min'er got up, he felt pain in his stomach, so he sat listlessly in a chair in a daze.

"What are you sitting here for? Are you feeling unwell?" his brother Cong'er asked him.

"I don't know why my stomach hurts so much today," he said, and went to defecate.

After a while, Min'er quickly ran out and said to his brother, "It's really strange, I don't know how I excreted a lot of worms, but my stomach doesn't hurt anymore. Brother, what are those worms?"

"That must be roundworms."

"What roundworms?"

"A roundworm is a parasitic animal. It often parasitizes in the intestines of the human body. At first glance, it is similar to an earthworm, but if you look closely, it has no segments on its body, so we call it a round animal. Its color is yellowish-white or slightly reddish, and both ends are thinner. The abdomen, back, and both sides each have straight lines. The one on the back is called the dorsal line, the one on the abdomen is called the ventral line, and the ones on the sides are called the lateral lines. This is the approximate shape of its appearance. But parasitic animals have general properties: (1) They parasitize in the bodies of all animals and absorb ready-made nutrients, so their digestive organs are very simple. And roundworms don't even have stomachs. (2) Their reproduction is particularly developed, and the reproductive power of roundworms is very alarming. It has been calculated that roundworms can produce 15,000 eggs in one day and night. (3) They parasitize in animal bodies, so their sense of feeling is very weak, because they are not needed. (4) Their heads have hooks or suckers, which can fix their position."

"Then what is the relationship between roundworms and us?"

"Parasitic animals mostly parasitize in the intestines of the human body, absorbing blood and nutrients. If the impact is small, it is stomach pain; if the impact is large, it will cause lack of blood in the body, headaches, muscle pain, loss of appetite, mental abnormalities, and other diseases, and even death. The impact of roundworms is relatively small. But there are always disadvantages."

"Then how do we prevent it?"

"They enter our body mostly directly. For example, the eggs of roundworms are excreted from the body with the feces of the animals they parasitize. If they are left in water or on vegetables, people will drink water or eat uncooked vegetables, so its eggs enter the body and develop in the intestines. So next time you eat something, you must be especially careful and never eat uncooked things."

Everyone Learns from Yuwen Shen 190

— Chen Tiewu

Ancient China, about to sink, watching the Central Plains being divided. The Simplest Gas Mask 191

— Jun Peng

Since the development of science, war has become even more terrible than before. Today's war is completely chemical warfare, and the most terrible of these is the release of poisonous gas. We should know that once a war breaks out, regardless of the front or the rear, the enemy can send a large number of bombers to attack our major cities or important resource areas, and release various poisonous gases to kill the people in the rear, restrain the soldiers fighting on the front, and give a major mental blow to the people in the non-toxic areas. Therefore, we must deeply study the knowledge of gas protection and how to implement protection methods. Here, I will introduce to you a simple method for making a gas mask. Little friends! Hurry up and make one to play with!

Method: Prepare a tin cigarette can. Punch two small holes on the edge of the lid for tying the rope. Then drill a number of small holes in the bottom of the can. Then go to the pharmacy to buy sodium carbonate and sodium thiosulfate, a certain amount of each. Mix them evenly with clean water, the thicker the better. Add a little glycerin to mix them. Soak the cotton wool in it. Put the soaked cotton wool into the finished can. The outside of the can must be covered with gauze soaked in this solution. In this way, it can be tied to the face to cover the mouth and nose, and become a simple gas mask.

There are also two simpler methods of gas protection, which are to soak the daily-used towel in clean water and cover the mouth and nose to breathe, which can prevent relatively light poisonous gas, and to wet the towel with soapy water, or use one's own urine in an emergency to cover the mouth and nose. This is what we can do very easily temporarily.

Little friends! Our gas mask is made, but we should know how dangerous we are! At any time and anywhere, the enemy can come to attack and use the most cruel means, so we have to prepare early, and gas masks are very expensive to buy. How can our poor common people afford them? Therefore, I hope that 200 million little friends across the country will quickly go to the poor rural areas to promote the gas mask here, which anyone can make. I think you will all be happy to take on the task!
