But, little friends, this is a time of serious national crisis. The borders of Suiyuan are being invaded by bandits, and enemy planes are constantly flying to drop bombs and bombard. The soldiers in the National Army are swallowing ice and chewing snow, fighting bloody battles, and Qingdao, a piece of pure land, has been trampled on by iron hooves. Shark (Part 1) 194

— Dong Xun

Q: Is a shark a type of fish? A: Yes, a shark is a cartilaginous fish, belonging to the squalus genus of the horizontal-mouthed class. Therefore, sharks are also known as squalus. Q: What is a cartilaginous fish? A: Of the more than 16,000 species of angular fish on Earth, they can be divided into two orders. One is the bony order. All fish belonging to the bony order have hard bones. The other is the cartilaginous order. They are the opposite of the bony order and are all cartilaginous. In addition, their caudal fins are irregular, with the upper lobe larger than the lower lobe. The body is covered with shield-shaped scales. The outside of the gills does not have a gill cover. The inside of the body does not have an air bladder. These are all unique features of cartilaginous fish.

Q: Then what is a "horizontal-mouthed class"? A: The horizontal-mouthed class is a type of cartilaginous fish. All fish belonging to this class have large and horizontally split mouths that grow on the abdomen. The nostrils grow at the lower end of the snout. There are five pairs of gill holes, but there are also six or seven pairs. Their juveniles are either viviparous or oviparous. Q: How big can the largest shark be? A: Among sharks, the long-tailed shark is the longest, at 15.6 feet long. The hammerhead shark is about 10 feet long. The rat shark is about 10 feet long. The cat shark is 3.4 feet long. The white shark, blue shark, and horn shark are all about 2.3 feet long. Q: Please tell us about the morphology of these sharks in general. A: Okay, now I will start talking, please listen carefully!

(1) Long-tailed shark: Its head is very short, the end of the mouth is round, the dorsal fin is very high, the pectoral fins are also very wide, and the length of the caudal fin is equal to the length of the trunk.

(2) Hammerhead shark: This shark is also known as the mallet shark, because its head grows protruding left and right, deforming into the shape of a double mallet, and also looks like the head of a mallet used to strike a bell in a temple, which is very beautiful.

(3) Rat shark: Its body is also very long, and the shape of its head is sharp like a rat, and its tail fin is very large. (4) Cat shark: The body of the cat shark is much smaller than that of the rat shark, which is exactly the opposite of the size of real cats and mice on land. At the same time, because its head shape and markings resemble a tiger, it is also called the "tiger shark." Its head is shaped like a hammer, and the end of the snout is blunt and round. The color on the back of the body is light brown and slightly red, with many dark brown and light brown horizontal stripes, like the markings of a tiger. The fins of this shark are very large, and there is a powerful hard spine at the front of each of the two dorsal fins.

Filial Piety (8) 196

— Hai

While travelling along the Volga River, the boat was being hauled by several horses on the shore. Suddenly, a very strong windstorm swept through. To keep the boat from crashing into the bank, the boatmen used a thick oar and accidentally knocked Perskovya and two other passengers into the river. Fortunately, they were soon rescued. However, due to a secret part of her body, Perskovya was reluctant to expose herself in public. The wet clothes, sticking to her body, further damaged her health. A friend trusted by Mrs. Milin separated from her in Novgorod. She continued alone, neither giving her a letter of introduction nor indicating the way forward, leaving her groping in the dark. Fortunately, the kind Mrs. Milin generously helped her, making her purse and luggage more full than when she first left Igish Village. The boatmen put her ashore at a pier under a bridge foot. She saw a chapel on a high ground ahead. As usual, she went there to pray before looking for a place to stay. The chapel was empty, but she heard the voices of many women behind a row of wooden grilles, praying. It turned out that this was a nunnery, and the voices of these women immediately gave her new encouragement and comfort. She thought, "If God can accept my prayer, I would also like to hide my face behind the veil like them, because I am very afraid of going to a hostel and being treated rudely." Having nothing to do at the moment, she began to pray again. A nun came and told her that it was time for the monastery to close. Please go out quickly. Perskovya immediately said to her that because she was unwilling to go to a hostel, could she be allowed to stay here for one night. The nun replied that they never received foreign travelers, but that their abbess might be able to help her. Perskovya opened her purse and showed it to the nun, explaining that she had received help from charitable friends in Ekaterinburg, and that she no longer needed any money, but only asked for a night's lodging. The nun was very happy with her generous attitude and took her to see the abbess. Her frank and moving story, coupled with the proof of her passport and the letter of introduction from Mrs. Milin, immediately made the gentle abbess excited and happy. She very diligently let her sleep in her own bedroom, and seeing the injuries she had suffered when she fell into the Volga River a few days ago, she decided to keep her for a few more days to recuperate.

After Perskovya had lived for a few days, she fell ill. Her illness was very serious, and the doctors said that her life had reached a very dangerous point. But although she felt that her illness was not improving, she was not disappointed. She said to herself, "I do not believe that my end has come, I hope God will allow me to complete my work." Sure enough, after a short time, she gradually recovered, although the recovery was very slow, lasting through the long summer. She was finally able to continue her journey. But her body after the illness was very weak and could not withstand the shaking of the post car, so she had to wait in the nunnery for a snow car to set off.

Special Report

Reply to Mr. Shen Zhenyi of the Bank of China: The Differences Between Domestic and Foreign Silk Price Calculations 213

Original letter, abridged: Recently, regarding the silk market report on February 4th, it stated, "The price difference between American and French silk and domestic silk is about 20 yuan." On that day (February 4th), the spot price in New York for 20-21 denier silk was between 78.20 and 78.21 cents, which, when converted to Chinese currency and deducting export fees, is approximately 790 yuan. However, the highest price for 20-21 white filature silk listed on the same day was 700 yuan, seemingly indicating that foreign prices are still about 90 yuan higher than Shanghai prices. It is presumed that the silk traded in Shanghai may be of lower quality. However, what standard of raw silk did your newspaper's reporters use to compare with the foreign market? Please clearly indicate this so that we may use it for reference.

(Reply) Regarding your inquiry, the following are the separate answers:

(1) The statement "The difference between domestic and foreign silk prices is about 20 yuan" in the daily silk news refers to a comparison between the price limits of goods wired from foreign countries to Shanghai and the prices held by Shanghai merchants. The silk grade should be the ordinary B grade.

(2) The reason why foreign silk prices cannot perfectly match the sales prices in Shanghai on the same day is threefold:

(A) There are many categories of raw silk. Even within the same white filature, 20-21 denier, the grades can be divided into GXX, Extra, Extra B, and ill grades. Those that cannot be divided include good A grade, good B grade, secondary A grade, secondary B grade, and so on. These grades are determined by the credit and output of their brands. Furthermore, the silk thread itself can be divided into direct-reeled silk, re-reeled silk, "Yangfan" (special reeled) and special "Yangfan." Due to the different silk threads, the prices also vary.

(B) The price of foreign silk needed to arrive in Shanghai includes the asking price of New York silk merchants and the price demanded by overseas buyers. This price has no standard. Therefore, the telegrams received by foreign merchants vary. Moreover, the exchange real-time market prices transmitted by Reuters inevitably have discrepancies. It is even more difficult to match them with the prices held or sold by domestic silk merchants.

(C) The export of Chinese silk is controlled by foreign merchants. It is common for them to be optimistic or pessimistic, release or suppress market prices. The foreign market prices reported in this newspaper are widely provided to silk merchants as a direct indication of foreign sales prices. Its correlation with Shanghai prices is only for reference and therefore cannot be the same as the Shanghai market's "signal" prices. Furthermore, the commissions deducted by foreign merchants also vary, making it impossible to generalize.

Supplementary Issue of Shenbao Local News: Amateur Weekly

Economic Exchanges

The Economic Construction of New Turkey 214

— Wang Defu

The new Turkey under the rule of Kemal is built upon these three principles: nationalism, secularism, and industrialization. As the first two are not directly related to this issue, they need not be discussed in detail. What we want to present here is the issue of the industrialization of new Turkey.

The past Turkey was based on agriculture and was a semi-colonial land under the joint invasion of European powers. After the end of World War I, especially after the victory over Greece, the new Turkish Republic under Kemal's rule since 1923 has strived for completely independent development in both economic and political aspects. Its most fundamental task is to transform an agricultural country into an industrial one.

However, according to the provisions of the Treaty of Lausanne, Turkey did not have tariff autonomy, which undoubtedly was a major obstacle to the economic construction of new Turkey. According to statistics from 1927, there were only 257,000 industrial workers in Turkey at that time, only three factories with more than 100 workers, and only 321 factories employing more than 50 workers. Their total horsepower was only 165,000 horsepower. As for the raw materials used by industry, they were only 232,666,000 Turkish pounds, and their production value was only 432,740,000 Turkish pounds. Among those factories, the main industries were agricultural industries, metal industries, textile industries, and wood industries; they accounted for 95% of Turkey's total industry. It was not until June 8, 1929, that the government's Grand National Assembly passed the protective tariff bill. This was the initial appearance of statism in the economy of new Turkey, and it was also a manifestation of its beginning to use the balance of foreign trade to seek its own economic independence.

In 1934, new Turkey further imitated the Soviet Union and formulated a five-year plan to implement a planned economy. The important points of this plan were somewhat similar to the Soviet planned economy, that is, to nationalize and operate important industries and pay attention to national defense construction. By last year, the Nationalist Party, Turkey's sole political party, had established a broad economic plan and issued the following declaration on industry: "All industries built for the purpose of Turkey's industrialization, whether private or state-owned, must follow the national plan. Turkish industry must not be partially concentrated, but must integrate the entire country. Therefore, the state must control prices and not allow cartels and trusts to raise prices for ordinary consumers." Regarding labor issues, it also stated: "In all economic enterprises, labor and profit must be harmonized by the state. Employers and laborers must be rationally controlled by labor laws." Such control is not only implemented in industry, but also for farmers. Turkish farmers must not be lazy. The government lends them money at minimal interest to enable them to cultivate land. At the same time, the government also urges farmers to develop underground resources, utilize hydropower, and control forests; and tells farmers, "National electrification is an important factor in the development of the motherland."

Under such an economic plan, Turkey's industries are divided into the following sectors: (1) textile industry (cotton, hemp, wool), (2) metal industry (iron, coal, lignite, copper, sulfur), (3) paper making and artificial ivory industry (paper, artificial ivory, rayon), (4) ceramics industry (ceramics, etc.), (5) chemical industry (sulfuric acid, chlorine, bicarbonate, phosphate). At the same time, there are the following decisions regarding investment in these industrial sectors (unit: thousands of Turkish pounds):

Cotton Spinning and Weaving 18,538

Wool Weaving Industry 11,650

Coal Industry 1,000

Sulfur Industry 300

Artificial Ivory Industry 1,025

Glass Industry 1,250

Chemical Industry 3,000

Hemp Industry 1,700

Iron Industry 10,000

Copper Industry 550

Silk 3,790

Rayon Industry 490

Porcelain Industry 800

From this, it can be seen that Turkey invests the most in the cotton spinning and weaving industry, followed by the iron industry; these two can be said to be Turkey's most important industries at present. According to the national economic plan, the estimated production volume of major industries is: cotton cloth 100,000,000 meters, hemp yarn 600,000 tons, woolen thread 1,000,000 kilograms, iron 100,000 tons, coal 60,000 tons.

Next is the finance of new Turkey. In order to implement such a planned economy, the Turkish government specially established a special bank in Ankara on June 2, 1933. This bank and the Turkish Bank are the main financial institutions of new Turkey. The former has a total capital of 20 million pounds, and its current capital is 6.2 million pounds; during the implementation of the five-year plan, the government will provide it with 6 million pounds annually; its important tasks are all national investment, distribution of products, control and guidance of economic construction. In terms of industrial investment, this bank is first engaged in the textile and paper industries. In the textile industry, this bank has established three large factories: the first is in Kayseri, the second is in Ereğli, and the third is in Nazilli. Among these three factories, the third can be said to be one of the largest and most modern factories in Europe. It has a total of 23,000 spindles, produces 30 million meters of cotton cloth annually, and consumes 560 kilograms of Turkish cotton. The number of spindles in the first factory is 25,000, and it produces 17 million meters of cotton cloth annually. The smaller second factory also has the capacity to produce 7 million meters of cotton cloth. Almost all of Turkey's required cotton cloth is supplied by these three factories.

This bank also invests heavily in the paper industry. Turkey's largest paper factory in İzmit was established with its investment. This factory alone will produce 50% of the paper needed in Turkey.

In addition, there is the iron industry, which is very important for both the national economy and national defense. This bank has been investing in its construction since last year and is currently planning its development.

As for the Turkish Bank, it was established as early as 1924, with only a capital of 1 million pounds at that time. Now its capital has increased to 5 million pounds (the pounds in this article are all Turkish pounds; please do not mistake them for British pounds). The investment activities of this bank first began in 1928 with the establishment of Turkey's earliest sugar factory. Its decision is to strive to invest in the mining industry, especially the coal industry. In 1926, it established the Turkish Coal Company in Zonguldak with a capital of 1 million pounds. Subsequently, it established a coal company in Kozlu, with an initial capital of 500,000 pounds, which was increased to 3 million pounds in 1929. Although this bank is nominally private, it is actually controlled by the Turkish Nationalist Party.

In addition to the above two major banks, there is also the Central Bank of the Turkish government, with a current capital of 160 million pounds. This bank undoubtedly controls important national financial functions.

What needs to be specially mentioned now is Turkey's natural resources and their development, which can be said to be an important foundation for the economic construction of new Turkey.

Turkey spans the two continents of Asia and Europe, with a population of 15 million and an area of 294,000 square miles. Speaking of its products, the richest are minerals. Its chromium and emery powder rank first in the world. Coal production is also very famous; Zonguldak on the Black Sea coast is the largest coal production area in the Near East. At the same time, Turkey is also working hard to exploit minerals; its coal production in 1923 was only 600,000 tons, but by 1934 it had increased to 2,180,000 tons. The production of silver is also considerable, about 8,000 tons per year. Although the production of sulfur is currently only 3,500 tons, according to the five-year plan, the annual production should be more than 1.5 million tons. The production of chromium, emery powder, manganese, and lignite was 120,000 tons in 1934, and of course there are still increases now. In addition, the production of copper, iron, and petroleum is also quite large.

Turkey's agricultural resources are also very rich, which can be indicated by the following figures (unit: hectare) —

Land suitable for cultivation 23,157,300

Valuable forest area 10,000,000

Pasture 27,000,000

Among the cultivated land, 90% is suitable for grain cultivation; and the area of wheat and barley accounts for 85% of it. The cultivated area of cotton is also increasing, and its center is in Adana.

Turkey is also a place where water vegetables are produced. Such as grapes, figs, olives, etc., it exports them every year. Under the provisions of the five-year plan, the output of these items has also increased significantly; compared to the past, they have increased by more than double.

In the economic construction of new Turkey, along with the development of general industries, railway construction has also achieved great results. By the end of last year, the railways built by the government had exceeded 6,000 miles; and it is planned to build 7,000 miles of railways from 1936 to 1940. If this continues, it will undoubtedly promote the further development of Turkey's economy. Of course, Turkey's economic development has not changed the nature of its society, but this is beside the point, and there is no need to discuss it here.

Biographies of Celebrities

Basil Zaharoff, the European Arms Merchant 215

— Zhou Jingxian

On the 27th of last month, death struck Sir Basil Zaharoff, who resided in Monte Carlo, the capital of the gambling country Monaco, on the French border. The life of Zaharoff was full of story-like mysterious legends. He was a famous "arms king" of Europe. His words could influence the politics of various countries and the fate of various nations. From his youth to his possession of absolute and immense authority, he was always regarded as a "mysterious person," and was feared and respected by some monarchs and great politicians in Europe.

There are many legends about his origins. According to official records, he was born in 1850. "Basil Zaharoff of Paris was his father." During the European War, British Prime Minister Lloyd George wanted to know more about the background of this arms merchant who was responsible for supplying the Allied countries with arms, so he entrusted the British Secret Intelligence Service to investigate. As a result, it was discovered that Zaharoff was born in Constantinople. His father was Russian, and his mother was Greek.

In his childhood, he was sent by his father to England for studies. In addition to studying English, he quickly learned French, Spanish, Italian, and Arabic. When his father passed away, he left him an inheritance of £40,000. After leaving school, he quickly gambled away almost all of his inheritance. The life of the following years is difficult to investigate. Some say that he drifted to New York and other cities in the United States and worked as a journalist, but this cannot be verified. His participation in international events did not begin until the early years after he turned sixty. At that time, he was supplying arms to Egypt and the upper reaches of the Nile.

Subsequently, he was appointed as the manager of the Vickers armaments factory in Athens, becoming an important figure in Greek political circles. His career as an arms merchant began in the Near East. He traded in all kinds of arms. He once served as the manager of the Vickers armaments factory in Paris, specializing in arms trade with Russia. It is said that during the Russo-Japanese War, he contracted to build warships for Russia and made a lot of money.

Although he was an arms merchant, he was also a politician in Europe. He often served as an intermediary between Briand and Lloyd George. Later, he shuttled between Lloyd George and Clemenceau, negotiating the politics of Europe between Britain and France. During that period, he was regarded as a "mysterious person," because he traveled between London and Paris, often traveling back and forth in the middle of the night, and his travels were all on a destroyer, crossing the English Channel.

One of the most story-like events in his life was what happened in Madrid, the capital of Spain, when he was over seventy years old. As he was coming down the grand staircase in the palace, he suddenly saw a young man in aristocratic attire grabbing a young woman by the neck and shaking her incessantly. So he rushed up and intervened. The young woman was knocked over and almost fell, so he embraced her with his arm. Unexpectedly, this young man was Duke Francisco, a member of the Spanish Bourbon royal family and nephew of the Spanish King. The young woman was the Duke's wife, Magina, who was only twenty years old at the time.

This was a very interesting scene. But from this scene, Zaharoff began to develop a friendship with the Duchess. Duke Francisco subsequently became mentally deranged, and his family imprisoned him in a villa in the suburbs. He died in 1924, and in that same year, Zaharoff married the Duchess and lived happily in Paris, Nice, and Monte Carlo. Unexpectedly, only eighteen months after the marriage, Zaharoff's wife suddenly died, which was a great blow to Zaharoff. From then on, he rarely appeared in public.

He had many residences. In France, the Villa Balincourt in Auberive was one of the most exquisite. It was originally the property of Prince Billya Paulte and is one of the most beautiful villas in France. All the artistic decorations were collected from all over France over forty years. All the furnishings inside are also very exquisite. There is also a pond behind it for Zaharoff to row boats. However, he always lived in Monte Carlo in winter. It is said that after the Great War, Zaharoff held immense power in Monte Carlo. In the Monte Carlo Grand Theatre, which was modeled after the Paris Opera, there were three special boxes. The center box was occupied by the Prince of Monaco, the left box was Zaharoff's, and the right box was reserved by the theater owner for members of the royal family and the owners of various casinos.

In middle age, Zaharoff was slightly taller than the average person and had a thin appearance. When he was eighty years old, he had a total property of £200,000,000. In recent years, the mystery of his life has increased and progressed with age. The recent burning of his diary is an example. His diary contained records of daily events and criticisms of contemporary figures. Fearing that it would be discovered by others after his death, he specially assigned six secretaries to sort it out and burn it.

He often gave away the colored paper from cigar bands to his friends as a sign of good luck. He also had some superstitions, but he was particularly superstitious about the colored paper on cigar bands.

Although he was one of the behind-the-scenes figures in the international community, the villagers near the Villa Balincourt did not know that he was the richest man in Europe.

Now Zaharoff is dead, and the secrets of his life will forever remain secrets. Some say that his career will end with this. But others say that even though he is dead, his power still exists. But what the truth is, I am afraid that only a very few people in the European political arena know.

Social Science Lecture

Evaluation of Cultural Sociology 216

— Zheng Yi

Sociology is a science that was established only a few decades ago, and cultural sociology is an even more recent product, established after the European War, and is still in its infancy. Therefore, not only are people generally unfamiliar with cultural sociology, some are even quite skeptical or even opposed to it, and some misunderstand it, but even those who consider themselves to be proponents or supporters of it have various opinions and cannot agree on a single view. This discipline (or rather, this school of thought) originated in Germany after the European War, and figures such as Max Weber, Durkheim, and Spengler all advocated it. Later, the United States inherited and responded to this view, and it became popular for a time. As for our China, it also followed the footsteps of the United States, bringing this newly emerging cultural sociology into this backward China from the "second-hand," and applying it widely, even considering it as its own discovery, such as Sun Benwen being its main figure. In Japan, figures such as Tanaka Odo, Miyauchi no Tasuke, Tsuda Sokichi, and Nishimura Shinji can all be said to be scholars of the cultural sociology school, both before and after.

Regardless of how many people advocate or support it, no one has yet systematically written a book on cultural sociology. Our understanding of it mostly comes from various magazine articles, or from incidental mentions in ordinary sociology works, and some sociology outlines or principles of sociology are simply written from the perspective of the cultural sociology school, but labeled with the name of cultural sociology, except for Kan Eikichi's "Cultural Sociology" in Japan and a few thin books like "Social Cultural Foundations" and "Cultural Theory of Sociology" in our backward China, there are practically none in the world. Because of this, it is necessary to give a simple description of what cultural sociology actually is, whether it is worthy of being called a science, and what its content is.

When we first see the term "cultural sociology," we cannot help but wonder: is this "sociology" or "cultural studies"? If it is sociology, then it can only be said that this is the sociology of the cultural school, like the sociology of the biological school, the sociology of the materialistic historical view school, the sociology of the idealistic historical view school, etc. How can we add the two characters of culture to the overall name of sociology? If it is cultural studies, then this is just a branch of cultural studies that studies culture from a sociological perspective, and cannot be called "cultural sociology." Therefore, generally speaking, cultural sociology does not fear how many people advocate or use it, but in reality, it is still an inappropriate term.

Furthermore, we examine the content of cultural sociology as defined by the cultural sociology school. As they say, "Cultural sociology is the study of understanding culture according to social regulations (modern German and Japanese sociology)." (See "Cultural Sociology") This is very unreasonable. Since it is "the study of understanding culture," then why is it called "sociology"? When we look at the content it lists, there is "the national character of culture," "the class nature of culture," "the time-bound nature of culture," etc. This proves that it is dealing with culture and not with society, and should belong to cultural studies and not to sociology. We also see Durkheim's "Sociology of Religion" and Scheler's "Sociology of Knowledge." Among these, such as religion and knowledge, all belong to culture, and the study of religion or knowledge is part of cultural studies, and their so-called "cultural sociology" is also a general name for cultural studies. But we also see Sun Benwen saying in his book "Social Cultural Foundations": "A group of people who have a common culture and therefore express common behavior is a society." "Without culture, there is no society; society exists in culture." "Society is the product of culture." In this way, the study of culture is sociology. Because culture is the mother of society and the foundation of society. As long as culture is studied clearly, society will also be studied clearly. Therefore, cultural studies is sociology. The reason why it is called "cultural sociology" is to distinguish it from other schools of sociology. Looking at Scheler's words again: "The pluralism of groups and cultural forms is the starting point of all sociology." He does not agree with the idealistic monistic sociology of German ideologues, and also opposes materialistic monistic sociology, believing that neither spirit nor matter alone is sufficient to explain the structure of society, and neither can determine the development of society. Only by taking various cultural elements, such as religion, philosophy, and other spiritual cultures, plus material culture, and having these various elements interact with each other, can we explain the development of society. From these points of view, the so-called "cultural sociology" is again sociology. In short, this term is not only theoretically incomprehensible, difficult to understand, and inappropriate, but even they themselves have not figured it out clearly.

Based on the above, regardless of what cultural studies is, summarizing the opinions of various schools, it takes various cultures, such as national character, class nature, time-bound nature, religion, knowledge, etc., as the spiritual and material elements of society, believing that the interaction of these elements constitutes society and determines the development of society. Compared with idealistic sociology and materialistic sociology, it is a pluralistic sociology. It does not only use spirit or economy to explain society, but also uses everything that should be available, such as nation, era, race, ethnicity, geography, climate, class, occupation, etc. to explain it.

We have explained "cultural sociology" very briefly, and now we want to evaluate it based on the object we are grasping.

As the cultural sociologists say: society is a chaotic mass, woven from various cultures, "society is the product of culture." Various cultures only have interaction with each other, but no determining effect. But according to science, the structure of society has its underlying foundation and superstructure. The underlying foundation is the economic structure, and the superstructure is the legal and political system and various ideologies. As for the so-called culture, such as capitalist culture, such as feudal culture, all kinds of thoughts and academic studies belong to the field of ideology, and are the superstructure of society. Scientific research is to explain fundamentally, to develop the causal laws, and merely mutual interaction — Please continue on the fifth edition.

Page 22

Page 23

is not enough. Culture is determined by the economic structure, which is known to everyone. As for culture being able to have a counter-effect on its superstructure, and causing interaction between each other, that goes without saying; however, the ultimate determinant is still its foundation, which is the scientific explanation. The task of sociology is to explain this structure of society and the causal laws of the evolution and development of this structure of society. In this way, cultural sociology not only cannot explain the true structure of society, but also does not know its laws of development. It has failed to complete the task of sociology at all. So whether it can become a science is still questionable.

Common sense

Who Made This Year's Harvest Abundant? 217

— Cheng

Everyone knows the name "bacteria," right? This thing that hygienists see as a venomous snake is the great hero that made our harvest abundant this year!

Don't believe it? Listen to me explain: In our country, farmers mostly use manure to fertilize the fields. When hygienists see it, they always cover their noses and pass by, saying it's unsanitary. But they don't know that all the food that fills their bellies needs, and is precisely cultivated by, these unsanitary manures. This is because manure contains the most chlorine, which meets the needs of plants. We see this manure sprinkled on the soil, and after a few days, it disappears, while the plants in the soil grow vigorously. At this time, if we examine it carefully, we will know that these manures must first ferment, decay, and be transformed into other substances before plants can absorb them. The bacteria that cause this manure to decay and change are the aforementioned hero. The ability of bacteria lies in their ability to make things decay. This is certainly harmful to the human body, but in agriculture, its contribution is even greater than that of cattle and horses. The chlorine in manure is contained in complex chemical compounds, so when bacteria arrive, they use their great power to make the manure decay. After that, the substances contained within are each decomposed, and after decomposition, they are each combined again, and then transformed into nitrate-like substances for plants to use.

The reason why soils are fertile or barren lies in whether there are many or few of these decaying things. The vast desert has no produce because bacteria do not like to grow there, which is due to the lack of humus. This kind of humus does not have a fixed composition, but through chemical experiments, we know that it is formed by the combination of organisms and minerals. In short, it is organic matter, containing the most protein. However, even with these humus materials alone, without the power of bacteria to help them ferment and combine, they are still of no benefit to crops. This is because before humus decomposes, its structure is extremely complex, and plants cannot directly absorb it. It must be fermented and decayed by bacteria, transforming complex substances into simple ones, and then, through several stages of bacterial fermentation, the nitrogen in the protein combines with other substances to become potassium nitrate or magnesium nitrate. These substances can then make plants thrive and develop.

This situation can be seen by observing the life of leguminous plants, such as peas and alfalfa. It can be known that the statement that bacteria are the heroes that make agricultural products abundant is definitely not false. If we pull up a pea plant to look at it, don't you see countless nodule-shaped things on those root hairs, some as small as mustard seeds, others as large as peas? If you try to remove these small nodules, the pea plant will gradually wither, and the peas that grow will also be small and few. What are these small nodules? They are packages of bacteria.

The growth of peas must require a large amount of nitrogen, which is to say, it needs a large amount of protein in plants. Although there is a lot of nitrogen in the air, plants themselves cannot freely absorb it, but the nodules on the root hairs of peas have this ability. They can grab a large amount of chlorine from the air and send it to the pea plant to use as nutrients.

The bacteria on pea roots not only help the growth of pea plants, but also turn barren soil into fertile soil. In Illinois, USA, there is a farm that specifically tested the effectiveness of bacteria on soil. They specifically divided the farm into three areas: A, B, and C. Area A was exclusively planted with corn, area B was planted with wheat or millet, rotating yearly, and area C was alternated with millet, wheat, or alfalfa, changing every year in a set cycle. After twenty-eight years, the yield of corn per acre in the three areas was twenty English bushels in area A, thirty-six English bushels in area B, and fifty-nine English bushels in area C, more than double that of area A! This is the contribution of bacteria on the pea roots.

The two most useful types of bacteria for plants are nitrite bacteria, which can convert the ammonia odor produced after the decay of substances into nitrite, and nitrate bacteria, which can take the chlorine in the protein of humus to create nitrate.

In modern times, with the flourishing of science, soil reformers often give a thumbs up and praise the effectiveness of their fertilizers. In reality, all fertilizers are nothing more than compounds with a large amount of nitrogen, and this nitrogen, like the nitrogen in the air, can absolutely not reach the plants without the help of bacteria.

Besides carbon, hydrogen, oxygen, and nitrogen, the growth of plants also requires calcium, magnesium, potassium, sulfur, phosphorus, iron, and other elements. But it is definitely not the case that plants can thrive by sprinkling those elements seen in the chemistry lab on the ground, because every element must go through the fermentation, decay, and manufacturing of bacteria before it can be used.

Because our country has reported good harvests in various provinces and regions this year, the villagers have flocked to temples to burn incense, thanking the Bodhisattvas for their protection. They do not know that the only hero that made this year's harvest abundant—bacteria—is still silently and inconspicuously continuing their work underground!

Sunday Literary Society

Zola and the French People 218

— Shi Fu

On the anniversary of the death of the French novelist Émile Zola this year, the French literary community held a meeting at Zola's former villa in Médan, near Paris, to express their commemoration. The Minister of Education, Talent, presided over the memorial ceremony and delivered a speech. He said, roughly, "The government is trying to improve the fate of the working class. The French working class has the virtues of thrift and peace. Zola knew this best and loved them most deeply." Zola was the leader of naturalism. Although he sympathized with the common people and workers of France in some respects, in the end, what he depicted was still "a world that French citizens created based on their own models." He himself was still a bourgeois figure. Now, the People's Front government in France, led by the Socialist Party, and a group of progressive literary authors in France, are holding a special meeting to commemorate him and say that he was the person who loved the French workers the most. This may seem difficult to explain, but upon closer examination, the meaning is very clear.

Zola was a French writer active in the latter half of the 19th century, and what he depicted was French society during the Second Empire and the Third Republic. Compared to Flaubert, Maupassant, and even all naturalist writers, he paid more attention to reality and worked harder to "expose the truth nakedly." He ruthlessly exposed the decadent lives of the French aristocracy at the time, accusing them of "treating prostitutes and street girls as the flowers of the nation" ("Nana"). He vividly depicted the greed of urban citizens and rural landowners (such as "The Belly of Paris" and "The Earth"), the fraud of a group of figures in the stock exchange ("Money"), and the pitiful and ridiculous vanity of the petty bourgeoisie who "buy bad beef but decorate the table with flowers" ("Pot-Bouille"). He opposed exploitation and expressed sympathy for the working masses, which can be clearly seen in "Germinal" and "Labor". In order to depict the tragic situation of the Franco-Prussian War, he created "The Debacle." In this, we can see his anti-war consciousness, although it is not very clear or thorough.

In 1894, under the sway of a crazed anti-Semitic consciousness, the French authorities basely fabricated some facts, alleging that Captain Alfred Dreyfus, a Jewish French artillery officer, was suspected of leaking military secrets to the Germans. Thus, the famous Dreyfus affair in French history broke out, which can also be said to be an anti-Semitic, so-called "Jewish peril" event. In this event, French political parties were divided into two major camps: on the one hand, the royalists and other anti-Semitic forces, who not only insisted that Captain Dreyfus was guilty, but also fundamentally opposed the republican system; on the other hand, the radical socialist party and the socialist party camp, who not only exposed the authorities' conspiracy to frame Dreyfus and protested against the anti-Semitic fanatics, but also fought to protect the republican system. The great writer Zola was living in France at this time, and he certainly had to express his opinion on this event that shook the country. So he wrote an essay to vindicate Captain Dreyfus and rebuke the unreasonable anti-Semitic movement. However, this result angered the French authorities, who immediately ordered his arrest, even forcing him to flee to England, until the Captain's wrongful case was clarified before he could return to his homeland.——Why do we not hesitate to describe this event here? That is because in this event, it can be fully seen how much Zola loved truth and justice, and it can also be seen how consistent his actions and his real life were with his creative attitude.

Generally speaking, the conscious citizens of France at that time still loved Zola, because their society still had the possibility of continued development, their lives still had a future, so they could still fairly face reality, and they were not yet hostile to Zola, who depicted objective reality. Moreover, although Zola depicted the ugly side of French bourgeois life, he was "seeking remedies for the shortcomings of the bourgeoisie in bourgeois morality" (Professor Cogan's comment on him), which should be especially praised by truly cultured citizens. Therefore, those who hated Zola at that time were not French citizens, but the French aristocracy, conservatives, and churches, etc. For example, the Catholic poets Barbey d'Aurevilly said that he was "a despicable artist" and ridiculed him as "a disgusting Michelangelo."

What about now? Capitalism has entered the final stage of its demise. In the course of history, the bourgeois class, like the aristocracy of the nineteenth century, has become a group of people who dare not face reality. What is expressed in terms of ideology is that Nietzsche's superman philosophy, new heroism, and mysticism have replaced scientific truth, liberalism, and realism. Thus, those who fear reality, oppose democracy and freedom, and oppose Jews are no longer the aristocracy that has been crushed by the wheels of history, but the bourgeoisie who are trying to stop the wheels of history from moving forward with their last efforts. This situation is particularly evident in Germany and Italy. As for the situation in France, although it is somewhat different from that in Germany and Italy, the financial capitalists, military industrialists, speculators in the stock exchange, and the followers of Colonel de la Rocque (leader of the Croix-de-Feu), are now inheriting the position of the French aristocracy of the nineteenth century, following in the footsteps of Mr. Hitler in Germany, working hard to oppose the republican system, oppose pacifism, and oppose the Jews, attempting to use new heroism and Nietzsche's mysticism to be enemies of truth and justice. If such a large French bourgeois presented all of Zola's literary heritage before them, they would never accept it. At this time, those who can promote his spirit of facing reality and loving truth and justice are only the French workers and progressive people. Therefore, those who commemorate Zola and give him the highest evaluation are not the great citizens of France, but the French People's Front and general progressive writers.

Of course, it is an overestimation to say that Zola knew the French workers "most deeply" and "loved them most deeply." From all aspects, we can only say that he was a progressive bourgeois writer, a reformist, because although he depicted the dark side of capitalist society, he did not fundamentally negate that social system, and he did not even know who would use what methods to reform that society. Perhaps the reason why the Socialist Party people overestimate him is precisely here. However, for the groups of people who can truly bear new historical tasks, everything about Zola must be accepted critically.

Manners and Customs

The Sex Life of African Natives 219

— Xiao Tian

Seven thousand concubines in the harem. From the perspective of modern civilized people, polygamy is unreasonable no matter what. However, in the evolutionary process of history, there was indeed a period when polygamy existed. At that time, women were completely slaves of men, private property: if a man had a lot of property, he could marry many wives and concubines. For example, a chieftain-like figure would often have several subordinates, rob several branches, have several heads of livestock, several leopard skins, several cowrie shells (currency), and the equivalent of these in wives and concubines. This situation still actually exists among the natives of Africa today.

The phenomenon of so-called polygamy is extremely common in the places where African natives live, and one can almost always see a man raising a large number of wives and concubines. For example, in the Bunya region of Uganda, most chiefs have ten to fifteen wives and concubines; even the poor have at least three or four wives and concubines. The rich of the Nandi tribe in the Kenya highlands have forty wives and concubines at any given time. In the Lezalis region of French Congo, there is a famous person called Berlin...
